1. INTRODUCTION
 This document is Volume 3 of the Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for
 Rogun HPP (also referred to as the Project). It defines the environmental and social measures that
 need to be implemented for mitigation of impacts and/or minimisation of risks for the environment,
 based on impacts and mitigation measures identified in Chapters 8 to 24 of this ESIA. The present
 version of the ESMP is based on the drafts originally prepared by WSP, the consultant who was
 mandated with preparing the ESIA.
 Activities during the construction and operation of Rogun HPP and the completion of the
 resettlement program (collectively, the Project) have been identified and assessed in Volume 1,
 Chapters 8 to 24 of this ESIA. Where activities with a potential impact on environment and social
 resources could result in effects of major or moderate significance, appropriate mitigation measures
 have been identified to minimise the significance of the effect.
 The principal objective of this Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP) is to
 “operationalize” the commitments to ESHS management and mitigation that are identified in Volume
 1, Chapters 8 to 23 of this ESIA.
 The main focus of this document is on the construction and operation phase of the Project.
 Mitigation of social impacts which are related to resettlement are dealt with in separate documents
 and are not included here.
 The ESMP is organised in the following way:
    •   Part A, Roadmap, describes the overarching guiding principles of the ESMP.
    •   Part B provides two sets of plans, namely:
            o   A series of detailed plans which can be directly implemented by the relevant entities; note
                that they may still need some adaptations in order to match the requirements depending on
                the conditions of the respective actor.
            o   A series of plan frameworks which deﬁne in broad terms the requirements to be met for
                reaching compliance with the relevant standards; these frameworks will serve as the basis for
                the contractors to prepare their own plans, and they will serve as the benchmark for
                acceptability of these plans by the project proponent.
 The ESMP describes the roles and responsibilities of all parties involved in Project construction and
 operational activities. ESMP implementation will require coordination of a complex Project
 organizational structure to ensure that construction and operating procedures are implemented
 throughout the procurement, mobilization, construction, and operational phases of the HPP and
 throughout planning and implementation of the resettlement program. Responsibility for the site-
 wide coordination is with Rogun JSC for the construction site, as delegated to the Employer’s
 representative.
 Ultimately, JSC will have the responsibility for the implementation of the plans. However, in most
 cases a different entity will be mandated with their direct on-site implementation. Foremost, this is
 the case for all site-specific plans related to construction, where the contractors will be in charge.
 JSC will assume its responsibility by closely monitoring all activities.

2. APPLICABLE STANDARDS
 Mitigation measures must be implemented in compliance with the laws of the Republic of Tajikistan
 and the Environmental, Social, Health and Safety (ESHS) standards of the World Bank and several
 international financial institutions (IFIs) (‘the Applicable Standards’). A detailed overview of the
 Applicable Standards is provided in Volume 1, Chapter 2: Legislation and Standards of this ESIA.
 These applicable standards include:
        Relevant laws and regulations of the Republic of Tajikistan law, including international
         agreements to which Tajikistan is a party;
        The World Bank (WB) Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) (2018) including the ten
         environmental and social standards (ESS), as well as the WB Group General
         Environmental, Health, and Safety (EHS) Guidelines (2007) and relevant Industry Sector
         EHS Guidelines;
        The European Investment Bank (EIB) Environmental and Social Framework (ESF),
         consisting of the E&S policy (2022) and revised environmental and social standards (2022);
        European Investment Bank (EIB) Environmental, Climate, and Social (ECS) Guidelines on
         Hydropower Development (2019);
        The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD) Environmental and Social
         Policy and Performance Requirements (PRs) (2019);
        Asian Development Bank (ADB): Safeguard Policy Statement (SPS) (2009) and associated
         safeguard documents;
        Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB): Environmental and Social Framework (2019,
         2021, and 2022); and
        Environmental and social standards, objectives and goals prescribed by other development
         financial institutions, including the Islamic Development Bank, the Eurasian Development
         Bank (EDB); the Saudi Fund for Development (SFD), and the Kuwait Fund for Arab
         Economic Development (KFAED).

3. ESMP STRUCTURE
 The Project E&S performance will be guided by Project-specific policies and plans that provide a
 structure to the management of ESHS risks. This ESMP provides the framework for the site-wide
 implementation of the management plans.
 The suite of full management plans and plan frameworks is illustrated in Figure 3-1; note that the
 plans listed under the heading of Social/Resettlement are separate documents not provided in this
 ESMP.
 The EPC contractors will develop their own, site-specific plans, which will have to comply with the
 requirements described in the Plans and Plan Frameworks provided in this document
 The key objectives of the management plans are to:
        Ensure all persons responsible for activities anticipate and take action to avoid impacts or
         risks to communities and the environment or to reduce them to acceptable levels;
        Support Rogun JSC and all contractors in complying with the Applicable Standards;
        Implement the mitigation hierarchy to anticipate and avoid, or where avoidance is not
         possible, to minimize, and, where residual impacts remain, to compensate or offset for risks
         and impacts to workers, affected communities, and the environment;
        Promote and provide means for engagement with affected communities throughout the
         Project life cycle on issues that could potentially affect them, and to ensure that relevant
         environmental and social information is disclosed and disseminated;
        Outline a process for monitoring and review the effectiveness of the procedures and
         methods and to take steps to promote continual improvement;
        Outline reporting and documentation requirements, and responsible parties; and
        Outline a requirement for management review.
 This ESMP provides support to the implementation of the management plans with:
        An E&S performance monitoring framework;
        An E&S performance reporting framework;
        A non-conformance and corrective action procedure; and
        A management of change procedure.
 In addition, the ESMP provides an estimate of the personnel and resources required for effective
 implementation of the E&S management plans.

This ESMP and full and detailed management plans will be “live” documents throughout the Project
lifetime and each full and outline management plan will undergo an annual, or more frequent,
review. Where necessary, amendments to the mitigation measures implemented by the EPC
Contractors or the subcontractors will be made to improve Project E&S performance where it does
not comply with regulatory requirements or the Applicable Standards.
This Document is organised in the following main way:
Part A: Roadmap. It contains the basic information on the role and content of the ESMP, covering
responsibilities for plan preparation and implementation, staffing, monitoring and reporting and the
overall ESMP budget.
Part B: Management Plan Frameworks, mainly those directly related to construction activities. These
Frameworks serve as the basis for the contractors to prepare their own Management Plans, which
will have to be specific to the site and to the work to be carried out by the different contractors.
Annex A lists a number of additional plans which are of importance for the implementation of the
Project while respecting all the relevant Environmental and Social Safeguards, which however are
separate documents not included in this present Report.

4. PROJECT ORGANSATION
 The Government of Tajikistan established the Project Management Group (PMG) for Energy
 Facilities Construction under the President of the Republic of Tajikistan as the implementing
 entity to oversee the construction and operation of Rogun Hydropower Project (Rogun HPP).
 Employer/Owner: OJSC Rogun HPP (Rogun JSC): responsible for ongoing operation of Rogun
 HPP and for construction of the Project. Rogun JSC provides supervision of Lot 3 EPC, Lot 4 early
 works contractors, other smaller contractors and of the Employer’s Representative, Tractebel ELC.
 Rogun JSC is ultimately accountable for all parties’ compliance with Tajikistan Law and, in future,
 International Standards.
 The Employers Representative (Tractebel ELC) provides overall supervision of E&S performance.
 The State Enterprise Directorate of Flooding Zone of Rogun HPP (DFZ) is responsible for
 implementation of the resettlement and livelihood restoration programs for communities and
 households displaced by the Project. They employ two main contractors, one for construction at new
 resettlement sites and another for demolition of relocated villages. DFZ also employs the State
 Forestry Agency to carry out land clearance works in advance of reservoir filling, and a contractor to
 transport property of resettled households to designated resettlement sites. It is also responsible for
 coordination with Government Ministries and Agencies as well as contractors that are involved in the
 resettlement process, including the reinstatement of the left bank road. Responsibilities and
 activities of this entity are defined in separate documents (Resettlement Plans and related
 documents) and are not part of this ESMP. Still, the plan frameworks for construction activities can
 be taken by DFZ’s contractors as a basis for their own site-specific plans.
 There are four main EPC Contractors and multiple subcontractors undertaking elements of the
 construction and operation:
        EPC Contractor for Lot 1: Voith Hydro GmbH & Co (Voith Hydro) is responsible for
         installation of four new generating units, delivery of two runners for two early generating
         units. Installation of the balance of plant and control equipment. Voith Hydro is expected to
         mobilise in early 2026.
        EPC Contractor for Lot 2: WeBuild (formerly Salini Impregilo SpA), responsible for
         design, procurement, and construction of the coffer dams and main dam, including
         treatment of the dam base (salt layer, grout curtain, drainage curtain).
        EPC Contractor for Lot 3: TajikGidroElectroMontazh (TGEM) responsible for a series of
         tunnels and spillways on the right bank that provide adequate flood discharge capacity as
         the height of the main dam increases, and lower tunnels can no longer be used for that
         purpose.
        EPC Contractor for Lot 4: the EPC Contractor has not been appointed to date but is
         expected to be awarded as soon after financing as practicable. The contractor will be
         responsible for the completion of works on the left bank.
 Lot 4 ‘early works’ contractors: two main contractors EMZ and Tunnel Sadd Ariana (Ariana) are
 implementing preparatory tunnelling and other works in advance of appointment of the Lot 4 EPC
 contractor. Both contractors will remain at the site after the appointment of the EPC contractor for
 Lot 4. Performance is supervised by Rogun JSC.

Other non-EPC contractors: Several smaller contractors (approx. 20 plus) are undertaking various
preparatory and maintenance works and are supervised by Rogun JSC.
The organizations currently responsible for ESHS management of the Project are presented in
Error! Reference source not found., which also indicated the supervision hierarchy for ESMP
implementation, which is as follows:
       PMG has the overarching responsibility, overseeing the activities of JSC and DFZ.
       DFZ oversees the performance of its contractors.
       JSC is responsible for ESMP implementation on the construction site; this role is largely
        assumed by the ER, acting as representative of JSC.
The Project organizational structure will change once there is a commitment to international
financing. The changes will include:
       A Project Management Consultant (PMC) ) reporting to Rogun JSC will be appointed to
        replace the Employers Representative to supervise all technical and ESHS performance for
        all contractors on site across Lots 1-4. They will report to Rogun JSC.
       In preparation for financing, PMG is tendering and selecting contractors for Lot 4. These will
        be awarded as soon after financing as is practicable.
       Lots 1 to 3 have been awarded to Voith Hydro, WeBuild and TGEM respectively, and are in
        construction or mobilizing to undertake the required scope of work.
       All “Early Works” contracts will be terminated except for Ariana and TMZ who will continue
        with the remaining early works pending the appointment of the new Lot 4 EPC contractor.

5. ESMP STAFFING REQUIREMENTS
 ESHS staffing for construction and operation is presented in Table 5-1 and Table 5-2
 respectively, including personnel for ESHS management planning, implementation, and
 supervision of the construction program (including the biodiversity “Clerk of Works” required
 by the Biodiversity Management Plan). Required DFZ staffing for the resettlement program
 is provided in the RPF and is not included here.
 In total, 355 personnel are required to implement the ESMP during the construction phase;
 and 24 personnel are required during the operational phase.
 Costs associated with the appointment of ESHS personnel and purchase of resources
 required for the implementation of the ESMP are provided in Section 13.

6. CONTRACTUAL REQUIREMENTS FOR ESMP IMPLEMENTATION
 The Project has, as part of the lender process, conducted a standalone ESIA which is additional to the Government of Tajikistan regulatory
 environmentally permitting requirements. The ESMP incorporates all mitigation measures identified within this ESIA that have been transferred
 into the full and outline Management Plans that are relevant to all on- and offsite locations where project activities are undertaken. This includes
 Project components and associated infrastructure.
 The contractual requirements for ESMP implementation are listed in Table 6-1.
 The ‘effective date’ is the date when the finance agreement between the World Bank and Republic of Tajikistan becomes effective.

7. MONITORING
 Monitoring of all the activities described in the ESMP has to be carried out in the way outlined in the
 respective Management Plans. The aims of the monitoring are the following:
    To check on compliance with the conditions set forth and standards to be met.
    To inform the relevant authorities (contractor's construction site management, Rogun OJSC) on
     cases of non-compliance observed.
    To propose corrective measures for such cases.
    To check on the success of these measures.
    To propose changes in the Plans and/or the monitoring system if controls reveal that the aims
     cannot be reached with the approach defined so far.
 Monitoring, in order to be effective, has to be done at different levels as described shortly below.
    The first level of monitoring will be conducted by the EPC Contractor or subcontractors in routine
     management of ongoing activities;
    The second level of monitoring will be done by the PMC/ER to periodically verify EPC Contractor
     or subcontractors E&S performance; and
    The third level of monitoring will comprise periodic auditing by JSC Rogun and PMG, using
     appropriately qualified personnel or contractors.
 Monitoring of effects and confirming the extent of implementation of the respective plans by the
 Contractor will be an integral part of the responsibilities of the ER/PMC as the Engineer to the
 Contract. This will be in addition to the Contractors’ own organization to ensure that the plans
 approved for each construction activity is implemented by their employees.
 The ER/PMC will be recording the performance on respective parameters for individual plans and
 construction activities for a consolidated report to the Project Proponent/Employer with their
 assessment of extent of compliance for each plan and respective corrective actions, where
 appropriate, with simultaneous sharing of this same information with the Contractors. Timelines for
 implementation of such corrective actions, where needed, will also be advised by the ER/PMC.
 Monitoring of progress on the works and such corrective actions will continue throughout the
 duration of each contract. The ER/PMC would also recommend contractual remedies included to
 ensure compliance, in case of persistence of such non-compliant activities. These may include
 temporary stoppage of work and/or withholding of (part of) payment/s due for that action or penalties
 or any combination of these as may be appropriate in the particular context of the non-compliance.
 More frequent monitoring and reporting may be required for certain activities, such as emergency
 operations (for instance at nights) or those that differ from the approved program. This will be done
 as per recommendation of the ER/PMC and agreement of the Project Proponent / Employer.
 Monitoring activities pertaining to each of the following frameworks/plans will be developed
 subsequently upon the operationalization of the respective plans.

8. TRAINING, AWARENESS AND COMPETENCE
 This Section provides an overview of general training requirements. Each of the site-specific
 management plans will include training requirements for the special topic of the plan in question.
 The following training must be provided, but is not limited to:
    Induction training – visitors to site that are either observing activities or undertaking specialist
     activities, such as field surveys, but will spend a limited time and are always accompanied, will be
     provided with introductory training to raise awareness of the site hazards and the precautionary
     measures to be observed for minimising the risks;
    Permanent personnel - personnel will be trained on relevant ESHS topics, including the jobs or
     activities they are to perform, the risks and impacts their actions may cause, and the measures
     they and others must take to avoid or minimize the ESHS risk and impacts.
    Specialist personnel - additional training will be provided to personnel according to the
     specialization of their role.
 JSC or, if mandated by JSC to this effect, ER, will develop and provide induction training to all
 visitors to the Project construction site. DFZ or their contractors (as required by DFZ) will develop
 and provide appropriate induction training to visitors to DFZ construction or demolition sites.
 Induction training for visitors and drivers will include, but not necessarily be limited to, a mandatory
 safety briefing covering:
    health and safety guidelines;
    location of first aid kits;
    PPE requirements; and
    any site-specific hazards related to their activities and/or locations visited.
 Each outline management plan includes a requirement for the EPC Contractor or subcontractor to
 prepare an appropriate training program that will be reviewed and approved by Rogun JSC. The
 training program will include training for site managers, ESHS managers and specialists, and
 supervisors and others who may be exposed to or cause risks and impacts.
 Training will include formal training sessions as well as regular “toolbox talks” undertaken prior to
 commencement of daily construction activities. All training will be documented, including the topic,
 trainees, trainer, location, date, and time of each session. Some training, such as for drivers or
 blasters, may require issuance of a certificate or license. Induction training for workers will include,
 but not necessarily limited to:
    Code of Conduct and social responsibility during construction, such as being considerate to local
     communities, community health, with a focus on the prevention of sexually transmitted infections,
     and gender specific requirements;
    Health and safety plans and procedures, including key occupational health and safety (OHS)
     hazards and controls on site;
    Management plans for which the contractor is responsible, including the Ancillary Works Plan, as
     appropriate;
    Incidents, non-conformance and corrective actions procedure; and
    Grievance mechanisms for workers and communities.




 Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment

Additional specialist training will be provided as needed to ensure understanding and effective
implementation of Project ESHS requirements; including training for drivers on the requirements of
both the off-site and onsite Traffic Management Plan (TMP).
Training Plans for PMG, DFZ, JSC Rogun and EPC Contractors will be developed and completed
no later than 3 months after the effective date, and training to be carried out throughout Project
implementation. The training modules will be developed with a focus on the various roles (e.g., EPC
contractors, DFZ staff, community liaison officers) etc. and include all necessary information and
guidance associated with the implementation of their roles on site. Furthermore, the training must
be delivered in a form and language accessible to the trainees to achieving the desired objectives,
Therefore, the training will be delivered in Tajik language (or at least interpreted if the training is
delivered in English), and all training materials will be available in Tajik.
Each organization will prepare training and competence matrices for the E&S roles to ensure that
training is comprehensive and focused.
E&S Training Plans will include:
   Stakeholder mapping and engagement;
   Specific aspects of environmental and social assessment, including management plans;
   Emergency preparedness and response;
   Community Health and Safety;
   Hazardous and Non-Hazardous Waste Management;
   Resettlement and Livelihood Restoration;
   Occupational Health and Safety;
   GBV/SEA/SH;
   Worker and external stakeholder GRMs; and
   Worker Code of Conduct.

9. ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES
 Responsibilities for ESMP implementation are organised hierarchically as described shortly
 hereunder.
 PMG: Has the ultimate and overall responsibility for ESMP implementation. This includes, but is not
 necessarily limited to, the following points:
    Preparation of the project-specific ESMP comprising plans or plan frameworks for all the relevant
     topics (the present document including plans related to resettlement, compensation and
     livelihood restoration).
    Checking of detailed plans prepared by the different entities; these site- and subject-specific
     plans must be accepted by PMG or, as the case may be, by JSC and/or ER (for plans related to
     construction activities and the construction site), and by DZF for plans related to resettlement
     activities.
    Checking detailed plans (if going beyond what is stipulated in this ESMP), and supervising
     implementation of plans which are neither related to construction activities nor to resettlement,
     and which will likely be implemented by contractors to be mandated specifically for these
     purposes. This mainly concerns the Biodiversity Management Plan (BMP) including No Net Loss
     (NNL), as well as the Cultural Heritage Management Plan (CHMP).
    Monitoring of implementation of all the Plans included in Parts B and C.
 DFZ: Responsible for implementation of ESMP standards and rules in all activities related to
 resettlement. This mainly applies to construction and demolition works required for RAP
 implementation.
 Rogun JSC: Responsible for ESMP implementation in all aspects related to construction activity
 and the construction site. This includes, but is not necessarily limited to:
    Including ESMP requirements and appropriate contractually binding wording in the tender
     documents for new contracts to be awarded, and change, to the extent required, existing
     contracts to make them compatible with ESMP requirements.
    Checking and approving site-specific plans prepared by contractors for their compliance with
     ESMP requirements; this includes timely preparation and implementation of these plans.
    In case of existing contracts: checking whether environmental and social protection measures
     already implemented by a specific contractor are in compliance with the ESMP, and making sure
     that such plans/measures are updated if this is not the case. Issuing a Note of Acceptance to the
     contractor for those cases where their plans/measures are deemed sufficient for fulfilling ESMP
     requirements, even if structure or wording is different to what is stipulated in the ESMP.
    Monitoring of implementation of all these Plans. Including tracking key parameters, the
     effectiveness of mitigation measures, and overall compliance and taking action as per the
     contractual agreement on continued non-compliance.
    Shall be responsible for implementing , monitoring, and evaluating the effectiveness of the Security
     Management Plan (Volume 3 of ESIA) and any associated security management sub-plans
     developed for the Project.

    Periodically carry out environmental, social, and health and safety audits to identify non-
     compliance and areas for improvement.

    corrective actions to prevent recurrence.
   Prepare and submit regular monitoring reports on the ESMP's implementation and results to
    project seniors, financiers, and relevant authorities.
   GRS Management
       o   Ensure continuous implementation of transparent and accessible grievance mechanism

   Submission of draft plans to the employer in a timely manner; finalising them by taking into

   In case of an existing contract, where EHS measures were applied, the contractor is required to
    submit the relevant information to the employer for deciding whether these plans/procedures are
    deemed to be in compliance with ESMP requirements, or where they need to be adapted for
    reaching compliance.
   Implementation of these plans.
   Direct and continuing monitoring of the effectiveness of the plans; updating them whenever

    performance of their subcontractors. This can be done
       o   either by requesting from subcontractors to prepare their own plans and have them
           validated by the contractor or the employer, or
       o   by clearly stipulate in the subcontracts that the subcontractor is responsible for carrying
           out all their activities in strict accordance with the contractor’s site-specific plans.
   In any case, the contractor has the obligation to monitor performance of its subcontractors and to
    ask for remedial action in case non-compliance is observed.
Every one of the entities listed above is required to have staff with relevant qualifications and in
sufficient numbers for implementing its tasks.
Personnel responsible for managing environmental and social performance must have the relevant
expertise and experience to undertake the necessary activities and tasks to comply with the
Applicable Standards.

       o   Provide job-specific induction training to all workers on ESMP requirements, safe practices,
           and the use of personal protective equipment (PPE) etc as outlined in the specific plans
           and Chapter 8 of this ESMP.

10. MANAGEMENT OF CHANGE
 The management of change procedure (MCP) sets out how the potential EHSS implications of
 changes to Project specific components, including dam design and hydropower configuration, and
 associated facilities, such as power lines, must be identified and assessed.
 Potential changes can be triggered at either the design stage, or during construction, and can be
 initiated by various stakeholders (PMG, JSC Rogun, DFZ, Lenders, members of the Community or
 the Contractor). Changes could be prompted by the application of the environmental and social
 design measures that are set out in the AWP, including but not limited to:
    Basic design refinement, after disclosure of the ESIA, due to detailed topographic or
     geotechnical information, or Lenders’ requirements;
    Detailed design development submitted by the design team of a Contractor in advance of the
     construction activities and approved by the PMC or, where resettlement related, DFZ;
    Results of further field surveys, investigations, and monitoring;
    Comments or concerns submitted by stakeholders, including the public;
    Changes in regulations or comments by regulatory bodies; and
    Unexpected issues arising during construction.
 The Contractor would define the technical amendments to the proposed design change for
 submission to PMC/ER or DFZ for a determination regarding the need to conduct EHSS studies to
 identify the potential E&S impacts of the design change.
 Three categories of change are identified:
    Category 1 – a design or activity change that does not result in any changes to, or impacts on,
     communities or the environment, and does not result in non-compliance with Applicable
     Standards. The impacts may be readily managed with mitigation measures outlined in the full or
     detailed management plans, if necessary.
    Category 2 – A design or activity change that could lead to E&S changes, but which are unlikely
     to result in significant effects. However, an appropriate E&S assessment would be required to
     demonstrate that the effect of the potential impact is not significant and to confirm that mitigation
     measures are already in place in the relevant management plans or AWP to minimise any
     effects that may arise. PMC/ER or DFZ would undertake a review and approve the scope and
     outcome of these Category 2 E&S studies prior to any design changes being implemented.
    Category 3 - a design or activity change that could result in a potentially significant effect, that
     was not included in the ESIA. Category 3 changes will require approval from both PMG and the
     Lenders of the scope and outcome of E&S studies. These E&S studies will need to demonstrate
     compliance with the Project E&S requirements. In some circumstances, the assessment may
     need to be undertaken in consultation with stakeholders and communities and may require full
     public disclosure, prior to confirmation of no objection by the Lenders, and will likely lead to
     changes to the relevant management plans. This change will come through either the
     Contractor, PMC, or DFZ who will prepare the MCP Form, including a description of the required
     E&S assessments, for submission to PMG for approval and submitted to the Lenders for
     confirmation that they have no objection. Work can progress once approval from PMG is
     received, and no objections are received from the Lenders.
 The MCP follows eight steps:



 Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
 Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                      October 2025
 Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                  Page 30
   Step 1 - the Contractor will notify PMC/ER or DFZ of the design change requirement and present
    details of the proposed change, the justification for the change, any alternatives considered and
    indicate their preliminary evaluation of the change category. The PMC/ER or DFZ shall review
    and approve the notification. PMC/ER or DFZ shall register all proposed changes to the design
    (irrespective of the entity who initiated the change) in an MCP log, for periodic review by
    PMG/the Lenders. The MCP log shall be used to document all design change decisions.
   Step 2 – the PMC/ER or DFZ shall examine the MOC Form and supporting documentation
    provided by the Contractor (e.g. drawings, technical notes, or Feasibility Studies) for all Category
    2 and 3 design changes to understand the features and location of the proposed change to
    confirm the categorisation of the proposed design change. If the PMC/ER or DFZ agree that the
    change is a Category 1 change, it will inform the Contractor, and no further work is necessary.
    PMG will be informed about all category changes in monthly reports. For all Category 2 and 3
    changes, the PMC/ER or DFZ will inform the Contractor of the need to provide a scope of works
    in line with Step 3 below. In addition, for each Category 2 and 3 design change, the PMC or DFZ
    shall assess whether the Contractor has evaluated sufficient alternative designs and selected
    the most appropriate option considering inter alia the potential E&S impacts.
   Step 3 - the Contractor is responsible for the procurement and funding of the E&S study
    necessary for Category 2 and 3 design changes (unless they are proposed by the PMC/ER, DFZ
    or PMG). The Contractor shall establish:
       o   the scope and level of detail of the necessary E&S assessment;
       o   the scope of any necessary site surveys; and
       o   the technical studies, assessments and reporting formats.
    The proposed scope of the E&S assessment will be based on the methods used in the Project
    ESIA, where applicable. PMG shall coordinate with the Contractor and PMC or DFZ to ensure
    that these needs are addressed. PMG will approve the scope of the E&S assessment for a
    Category 2 change via the review and monitoring undertaken by the PMC/ER or DFZ.
    For Category 3 changes, the PMC/ER or DFZ will review, monitor and inform PMG, and PMG
    shall report to the Lenders to inform them of: the proposed change; the result of the E&S
    screening; and to gain approval for the proposed scope of the E&S assessment/s. The E&S
    assessment proposed by the Contractor must comply with the Project E&S requirements. The
    Lenders must approve the scope of all Category 3 E&S assessments. At this scoping stage, the
    need for stakeholder engagement and public disclose of the final E&S assessment is also to be
    determined by PMG and approved by the Lenders.
    The PMC or DFZ shall review the Contractors proposals for:
       o   Scope and level of detail of the necessary E&S assessment;
       o   Scope of the site surveys;
       o   Technical studies, assessments and reporting formats; and
       o   Proposals for stakeholder consultation and public disclosure (where relevant).
    PMG shall review the proposed scope of E&S assessment based on the recommendation from
    the PMC/ER or DFZ to ensure it is compliant with the Project E&S requirement. For Category 3
    changes, PMG shall report to the Lenders the proposed design changes, the result of the E&S
    screening as per the MOC Form, the proposed scope of the E&S assessment and the strategy
    for stakeholder consultation. PMG shall inform the Contractor of the outcome of this review.



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                 Page 31
   Step 4 – for Categories 2 and 3 change, the Contractor procures, funds, and undertakes the
    approved E&S assessment for design changes. PMG would fund the E&S assessment if the
    changes are proposed by PMG. For Category 3 changes, the Contractor must undertake the
    agreed stakeholder consultation. The PMC/ER or DFZ will monitors the stakeholder consultation
    process and the E&S assessment. Where public disclosure and consultation of the E&S
    assessment is needed, PMG shall support the Contractor with any public disclosure and
    consultation requirements of any E&S assessments by organising public meetings and posting
    details of the disclosure on the Project website. Public disclosure and consultation will occur
    after Step 5 which is the review and approval of the E&S assessment. Feedback from disclosure
    and consultation shall be accounted for in the final design of the change.
   Step 5 - for Category 2 design changes, the E&S assessment report/s shall be submitted for the
    approval of PMG only. For Category 3 changes PMG shall provide the E&S assessment report/s
    for the Lender’s review and approval. The Lender’s must approve all Category 3 design
    changes. The review and approval of Category 3 changes must demonstrate compliance with
    the Project E&S requirements. The PMC/ER or DFZ will review, monitor the E&S assessment
    carried out by the Contractor, and give feedback to PMG. PMG shall inform the Contractor about
    the final outcome of the review of the design changes and the results of any E&S assessment
    reviews making clear the details of any additional work needed to the E&S assessment.
    Changes and updates will be made to the ESMP, or AWP if appropriate, as required for both
    Category 2 and 3 changes – see Step 7.
    The PMC/ER or DFZ shall review the Category 2 and 3 E&S assessment report(s) provided by
    the Contractor and verify the following for the final approval of PMG;
       o   Robustness of the baseline description;
       o   Relevance and adequacy of the impact assessment;
       o   Effectiveness of the proposed mitigation strategy; and
       o   Identification of any changes to the AWP or ESMP.
    Once any Category 3 EHSS studies are finalised and approved, PMG shall support the
    Contractor with any public disclosure requirements of any E&S assessment by organising any
    public meetings and posting details of the disclosure on the Project website.
   Step 6 - the PMC/ER or DFZ shall, for all approved design changes, carry out a review of
    existing permits to determine whether these could be affected. The PMC/ER or DFZ would be
    responsible for notifying the appropriate regulators of all material design changes where these
    could affect the terms of permits already issued, and the preparation of any revised permit
    applications. The Contractor will then be responsible for implementing and complying with the
    requirements of the local permits.
   Step 7 - if an approved design change requires environmental and social measures which are
    not covered by the existing ESMP or full or detailed management plan, the Contractor shall
    prepare an addendum to the ESMP and specific management plans to address any new
    mitigation measures. The addenda, together with the document, shall be submitted to the
    Lenders and disclosed on the Project website.
   Step 8 - for each approved design change regarding resettlement, DFZ shall conduct the land
    surveys required and the necessary consultations to update the Resettlement Framework (RF)
    for the area affected by the proposed change. The DFZ shall use the result of the RF
    investigations to minimise impacts on livelihoods and implement the required actions with the
    Contractor. The DFZ shall submit the addenda to the RF to the Lenders before payment of
    compensation and actual land take. The RF shall be disclosed on the Project website and
    compensations paid in order that the land take can be formalised.

11. INCIDENTS, NON-CONFORMANCES, AND CORRECTIVE
    ACTIONS
 Incidents would need to be recorded by the Contractors’ site personnel for purposes of maintaining
 conformity with the ESMP provisions. They would also provide sound basis for training and learning
 for subsequent stages of the work where repetitive activities are envisaged.
 When incidents come to the attention of the ER/PMC, they should be systematically documented for
 reporting to the project Proponent/Employer. In case of undocumented incidents being brought to
 the attention of the ER/PMC, appropriate measures may include requiring the contractor/s to
 undertake corrective measures as per the contract or advising Project Proponent / Employer to
 undertake necessary steps to ensure that ESMP objectives are met.
 In case of non-conformances to the Contract, the appropriate remedial measures would be
 recommended by the ER/PMC. As Engineer to the Contract, these would be binding for all
 concerned entities.
 Corrective Actions would be undertaken by the relevant actor to bring back activities to conforming
 status. This may include deployment of additional resources and/or removal of undesirable
 actions/effects that may require additional time and/or resources. These would be treated in line with
 the stipulations in the contract and be subject to same processes for appropriate remedies, if the
 concerned party is not satisfied with the outcome.




 Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
 Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
 Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page 34
12. ESHS REPORTING
 EPC CONTRACTOR AND SUBCONTRACTOR
 EPC and subcontractor will provide timely and accurate reports on ESMP implementation, in line
 with the respective plans, to the ER/PMC in formats agreed as part of the Contract. The Contractor
 will maintain the copies of the relevant regulatory permits and key information, including copies
 when requested.
 JSC ROGUN, DFZ AND PMC
 PMC will consolidate these reports on monthly basis and provide an analysis for reporting to the
 Employer / Project Proponent, along with their recommendations for further actions. In case of non-
 compliance/incidents, separate specialized reports may be needed, depending on the seriousness
 of the situation. Copies of these will be shared with the respective Contractors where appropriate.
 These reports can also be used for training of staff across the various actors to ensure that learning
 is applied to improve the project’s ESMP performance.
 JSC Rogun and DFZ will report quarterly to the PMG on the progress in the implementation of the
 ESMP. Their recommendations will be also shared with the ER/PMC and where appropriate with the
 Contractor.
 PMG
 PMG will provide semi-annual reports to the financiers describing the progress in implementation of
 the ESMP. Whenever requested, detailed PMC reports will also be provided..
 SIGNIFICANT ISSUE REPORTING
 In addition to scheduled reports, specific incidents such as fatalities related to site work or involving
 site personnel would require off-cycle and urgent reporting to ensure prompt implementation of
 mitigation measures consistent with requirements of the Project. These include notification to World
 Bank, and where needed other financiers, within 48 hours of any such incident coming to notice of
 the PMG.
 Subsequently, additional diagnostic work, such as root cause analysis, would be required to be
 undertaken in line with the recommendation/s of the ER/PMC and/or other stakeholders such as
 regulatory authorities, financing partners, etc.
 These reports would need to be completed in a timely manner and findings of these would inform
 the subsequent revisions of the respective plan/s, either at the time of pre-arranged review or off-
 cycle depending on the findings of such diagnostics.
 These reports could also inform training and building capacity of the stakeholder identified in Section
 8 above.

14. ASSOCIATED FACILITIES
 This ESMP incorporates all facilities supported by the Project, including those defined as associated
 facilities in accordance with the World Bank Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) and other
 applicable standards. Associated facilities are infrastructure elements and services that are not
 financed as part of the main project but are essential for its viability and functionality (e.g.,
 transmission lines, substations, access roads, and resettlement sites).
 DEFINITION AND SCOPE
 Associated facilities are identified in Volume 1, Chapter 3: Project Description. These include:
        Transmission lines (500kV and 220kV)
        Substation expansions
        Access roads
        Resettlement and livelihood restoration sites
 COMPLIANCE STATUS AND LEGACY FACILITIES
 Most associated facilities constructed to date have been subject to an Environmental and Social
 Impact Assessment (ESIA) that is compliant with the Applicable Standards. However, the following
 infrastructure was not subject to an ESIA prior to construction:
        The two 500kV lines and substation expansion at Dushanbe (completed in 2018)
        The two 220kV lines to Rogun City (completed in 2024)
 For these legacy facilities, an audit to confirm compliance with Applicable Standards must be
 undertaken as soon as practicable. The audit should assess environmental and social risks, identify
 any gaps, and recommend corrective actions to align with current ESMP requirements.
 FUTURE ASSOCIATED FACILITIES
 Any future associated facilities, such as the planned additional 500kV reserve line, will be subject to
 an environmental assessment in line with relevant requirements prior to construction.
 BUDGETARY AND MANAGEMENT RESPONSIBILITIES
 The budgetary consideration of the E&S impacts and their management for associated facilities will
 be handled by the respective project proponents. However, the mitigation measures and
 performance standards set out in this ESMP will apply and serve as the benchmark against which
 the E&S performance of all associated facilities will be assessed.
 MONITORING AND REPORTING
 The Project Management Group (PMG) will ensure that monitoring and reporting requirements for
 associated facilities are consistent with those for the main project. This includes:
        Regular compliance audits for associated facilities
        Integration of associated facility performance in semi-annual project reports
        Tracking and follow-up of corrective actions for any identified non-compliance
    Public consultation and disclosure of relevant E&S information


 Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
 Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
 Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                Page | 40
15. THE CASE OF ROGUN HPP: ESMP IMPLEMENTATION IN AN
    ONGOING PROJECT
 The ESMP, as a general rule, is prepared as a part of the ESIA and serves the purpose of defining
 in sufficient detail the obligations of contractors and other relevant stakeholders for implementing the
 project in compliance with the relevant legal requirements, guidelines and standards in order to
 minimise negative environmental and social impacts. The Management Plans and Management
 Plan Frameworks provided in the ESMP form the basis for the stakeholders mentioned for
 formulating their own site-specific plans.
 The two areas with the highest risk for negative impacts are the following:
        Impacts caused by the fact that, especially in the case of a hydropower project with a large
         reservoir, potentially a large number of people are directly or indirectly affected, and that
         there is a need for detailed planning with the aim of avoiding, minimising and compensating
         these impacts. This is done by means of the resettlement process, which is defined by a
         number of documents and plans like the Resettlement Action Plan (RAP), the Livelihood
         Restoration Plan (LRP), the Stakeholder Engagement Plan, etc.
        Impacts potentially caused by or related to construction site activities. The construction
         period is the project phase where most effects (on the physical and biological) environment
         happen, or where the risk for such negative impacts is highest; this includes impacts on a
         potentially large number of people, namely those involved in any way in the construction
         process as such, and here mainly the work force on site. A substantial number of the plans
         included in the ESMP aims at optimising all processes related to construction in order to
         prevent impacts from materialising and to reduce the risks to the extent possible.
 For being effective, it is important that these plans are ready at the moment when construction work
 starts. Usually the ESMP, and the Plans and Plan Frameworks related to construction, are part of
 the tender documents, giving the potential contractors a clear picture of the EHS-related conditions,
 at the same time clearly defining the obligation to prepare these plans ahead of mobilising the work
 force and starting with major work on site.
 The situation of Rogun HPP is different. As described in the ESIA, the project has a long history,
 and major work started in the eighties, but was then interrupted by the end of the Soviet Union, the
 independence of Tajikistan and the development following these events.
 Of special importance is the fact that full-fledged construction efforts resumed in 2016.
 These contractors, if they continue to work on site, will have to comply with the requirements
 stipulated in the ESMP. They will be given time for developing the respective plans. It is expected
 that especially the main contractors already have their own specific plans and implementing
 structures in place. They will have to show to what extent these are able to fulfil the requirements.
 Where this is not the case, updates will have to be made, or specific site-specific plans will have to
 be prepared.
 For all new contractors, or in the case of new contracts with already active contractors, full
 compliance with ESMP will be required, and this includes the necessity to have the plans ready
 before work starts.
