37. ON-SITE TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT PLAN
 BACKGROUND
 This Offsite Traffic Management Plan (TMP) Framework sets out a set of generic requirements for
 traffic management during the construction and operation phases of the Project. It provides general
 guidelines, principles steps and Good International Industry Practices (GIIP) that can be adapted to
 the project-specific traffic management plan as part of the overarching Environmental and Social
 Management Plan (ESMP) and other relevant environmental and social risk due diligence
 documents of the project. Accordingly, the objectives of this framework TMP include but not limited
 to establish general requirements of traffic management to be implemented by the project proponent
 and contractor to avoid and minimize traffic disturbance and ensure the safety of public and project
 workers during the project construction and operation.
 This TMP Framework is intended to be used for traffic management during the construction and
 operation stage of a project which may have potential impacts on road traffic and related
 public/worker safety concerns caused by road traffic. These include e.g. direct road construction or
 maintenance, construction activities occupying road or sidewalk, construction vehicles/equipment
 entering public roads, and construction vehicles/equipment through local community roads, etc.
 During the preparation, construction and operations, a project onsite -specific traffic management
 plan using this TMP as a general framework, taking into account project-specific situation and
 demand, will be developed as part of the project’s Contractors ESMP or other E & S documents as
 appropriate. In addition, during the implementation of the project, this TMP (or the project contractor
 specific TMP) will be incorporated into the bidding documents and latterly the construction contracts,
 as part of the environmental and social management specifications.
 Purpose and Applicability Traffic Management Plan Framework
 Each Contractor employed at Rogun Hydropower Project (the Project) will prepare and implement a
 Traffic Management Plan or Contractor’s Traffic Management Plan (TMP or C-TMP) that is
 consistent with this TMP Framework. The Plan will be reviewed and approved by the Contractor’s
 Project Manager and submitted to the Employer’s Representative (ER) and/or the Project
 Management Consultant (ER/PMC) for review. Once approved, it shall be diligently implemented by
 the Contractor.
 New Contractors must have an approved Plan before mobilizing workers. Existing Contractors must
 have an approved Plan within six months of the date that World Bank financing is provided to the
 Project or as otherwise required by the contract. If an existing Contractor has a TMP that has been
 approved by the ER, a new plan is not needed if the ER verifies the existing plan is equivalent to
 what is required by this Framework, or if the Contractor makes sufficient changes to the existing
 plan that the ER determines it is equivalent.
 The purpose of this TMP Framework is to identify the minimum requirements for the Contractors’
 TMPs, and to ensure the Plans contains the required content, although the Plan may vary based on
 the potential traffic hazards and risks of the works the Contractor is required to perform.
 SCOPE
 This On-site Construction and Operation On-Site Traffic Management Plan Framework is a
 reference guide for contractors to prepare, implement and manage traffic at their construction sites


 Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
 Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
 Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 179
through sharing some good practices. This framework TMP is not intended to be a duplication of the
Traffic and Transport assessment nor a substitute to Contractors TMP. However, this framework
TMP does not apply to areas outside the construction workplace where the contractor has no
management control and for which a separate TMP has been prepared for Offsite Traffic. This TMP
Framework should be read in conjunction with the following documents/reports:
      On-Site Traffic Management Plan (Volume 3, A9a)
      Security Management Plan (Volume 3, A7)
      Occupational Health and Safety Management Plans prepared by Contractors to meet
       requirements of Rogun JSC’s OHS Management Plan Framework
      Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP) (Volume 3, A1)
OVERVIEW
This Traffic Management Plan (TMP) Framework establishes the requirements for vehicle and traffic
management at the Rogun Hydropower Project (HPP) (hereinafter referred to as ‘the Project’). It
provides guidelines for contractors to ensure safe and efficient site traffic operations in alignment
with national regulations and project-specific safety protocols. This plan will be detailed and tailored
to the specific needs of each contractor involved in the project. Each Engineering, Procurement, and
Construction (EPC) contractor will develop detailed traffic management plans for their respective
areas and activities.
The Government of Tajikistan established Rogun JSC to own and operate the Project. The Project
Management Group (PMG) for Energy Facilities Construction, under the President of the Republic of
Tajikistan, is the implementing entity responsible for managing the construction of the Project.
Rogun JSC oversees both the construction and long-term operation of the Project, which is currently
undergoing an extensive phase of construction and partial operation, with two turbines already in
service .
Many parties associated with the Rogun Hydropower Project (HPP) operate vehicles and equipment
both on and off-site. These include PMG, Rogun JSC, the Employer’s Representative, multiple
contractors, consultants, and other stakeholders.
The Project involves extensive vehicle and equipment movement across more than 100 km of on-
site roads, as well as frequent transport to and from Dushanbe and other locations in Tajikistan.
Given this complexity, there is a need for consistent requirements governing vehicle operation and
maintenance to ensure safety, efficiency, and regulatory compliance across all Project activities.
Traffic Management And ESIA Alignment
This On-site Traffic Management Plan Framework (hereafter referred to as ‘TMP’) defines the traffic
management framework for the Project. While the strategy may be referenced in Volume 3, A1:
Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP), this TMP serves as the framework document
outlining the specific requirements, controls, and implementation measures for managing site traffic.
It establishes the necessary protocols to ensure safe, efficient, and compliant traffic operations
across the Project in lieu of each Contractor’s on-site Traffic Management Plan (CTMP).
The TMP Framework builds upon the existing Traffic Management Plan by incorporating findings
from evaluations of current on-site traffic practices. Conducted in consultation with Rogun JSC, the
Security Department, Contractors, and the Employer’s Representative, these evaluations identified



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 180
areas requiring refinement to enhance safety, efficiency, and compliance. The updated TMP
framework ensures alignment with Project objectives, regulatory requirements and site-specific
operational models.
A second plan, the Off-Site Traffic Management Plan (hereafter referred to as ‘OS-TMP’), will
address traffic interactions beyond Project boundaries, including the use of public roads, transport of
oversized loads, and worker travel. Together, these plans establish a cohesive framework to
manage traffic risks, optimize transport operations, and safeguard workers, contractors, pedestrians
and the surrounding community.
The TMP is a comprehensive document designed to ensure the safe and efficient movement of
traffic during the project's construction and operation phases. It involves detailed planning,
implementation, and monitoring to minimize the impact on local communities and the environment.
The plan is a critical component of the project's overall environmental and social management
framework, ensuring compliance with international standards and best practices.

SITE CONDITIONS
Site Location
The Project is located in an area that is sparsely populated, with limited agricultural activities in
nearby villages and predominantly undeveloped land. Rogun HPP is the uppermost plant in a
cascade of hydropower facilities on the Vakhsh River, situated upstream of Nurek, Baipaza,
Sangtuda 1, Sangtuda 2, and Golovnaya HPPs.
The region experiences a continental climate with cold winters and hot, dry summers. Seasonal
weather variations affect road conditions, with hazards such as slippery surfaces, flooding, and
landslides during winter snowmelt and spring rains. These factors are integral to the traffic
management strategies outlined in this TMP.
The Rogun dam site is located in a narrow gorge with steep flanks, approximately 6.5 km from
Rogun town. The project site is in the Rasht region, affecting three districts: Rogun, Nurobod, and
Rasht. The construction site occupies an area of about 20 km² both upstream and downstream of
the dam site near Rogun town.
Additional details on the site location and project background are available in the Volume 1,
Chapter 1: Introduction of the ESIA.




Figure 37-1: Road network in the Project area
                Source: Figure 3-1 from 2014 ESIA
Key Site Features
The TMP applies to all construction zones, access roads, tunnels, and temporary facilities
associated with traffic movements at the Rogun HPP site. Key features include:
      Dam and Reservoir: The dam currently reaches 1,110 m above sea level (m asl), with the
       reservoir currently at 1,075 m asl, with the full elevation of 1300 masl expected by 2032 and
       full reservoir capacity at 1290 masl expected by 2038.
      Powerhouse and Turbines: The underground powerhouse currently operates two turbines,
       with plans for four additional turbines to be installed in phases.
      Access Roads and Tunnels:
       o   Underground Roads: Approximately 70 km provide internal access.
       o   Aboveground Roads: About 26 km, mostly unpaved, connect surface areas.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                        October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                  Page | 183
         o   Water Tunnels: Around 15 km serve water management needs, with some of them
             currently serving as roadways pending filling of the reservoir.
        Temporary Construction Facilities: Facilities include borrow pits, spoil storage, batching
         plants, logistics hubs, and laydown areas.
        Construction Camp and Traffic Infrastructure: The main camp, near Rogun City, is
         planned for relocation as reservoir levels rise.
        Operational Buildings and Contractor Camps: Permanent offices and contractor camps
         support long-term needs and on-site housing.
        Vehicle and Equipment Maintenance Facilities: Workshops operated by Rogun JSC and
         contractors provide maintenance and servicing for construction vehicles and heavy
         equipment.
        Village Settlements: Several villages within the project boundary are undergoing
         resettlement to new locations.
Further details on Project site components are available in Volume 1, Chapter 3: Project
Description.
Site Access
Main Site Access Gate

1.1.1.    The primary access point to the Rogun HPP site is the main gate, situated on the western
          boundary at a lower elevation near Rogun City. It connects directly to the M41 highway,
          facilitating transport to and from Dushanbe and surrounding regions.
1.1.2.    The gate serves as the central control point for vehicles, equipment, and personnel entering
          the construction and operational zones. Access is strictly regulated through three levels of
          security checks conducted by national army personnel, police, and Rogun HPP security.
1.1.3.    Entry is granted only to individuals presenting pre-approved access cards or permits,
          issued under a controlled permit system applicable to all personnel, including Project
          personnel and visitors. Security personnel are required to verify access cards at this
          checkpoint.
1.1.4.    The majority of site traffic, including materials transport, delivery trucks, and pedestrian
          workers, passes through this gate. Key infrastructure includes guardhouses, automated and
          spike barriers, and traffic control signage, ensuring regulated entry and maintaining site
          security. Figure 5-1 illustrates the layout of the main access gate.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 184
Main Site Access Gate
Secondary Site Access: Secherogh (“Sicha-Rogh”) Bridge

1.1.5.   The secondary access point, known as the Secherogh Entrance, is located to the northeast
         of the Project site boundary. This route crosses the reservoir via a temporary, one-way
         suspension bridge with a speed limit of 10 km/h. It connects the east bank stockpile and
         crushing area to the west bank, providing access along an existing road that ascends the
         embankment towards Rogun City and Construction Site 2 from the north.
1.1.6.   This access route is significantly less active than the main site entrance, managing a lower
         volume of traffic. Security is controlled by Rogun security personnel with assistance from
         the national army and police, and entry is regulated through verification of pre-authorized
         personnel access cards/forms at the checkpoint. Figure 5-2 illustrates the Secherogh bridge
         structure.
1.1.7.   The Secherogh bridge is a temporary structure that will be dismantled prior to the reservoir
         rising to elevation 1,100masl,scheduled forlate 2025 or 2026. In the meantime, the only
         non-construction traffic allowed over the bridge is for residents of two villages on the left
         bank, who will be required to use bridges farther upstream when this construction bridge is
         dismantled and who have been issued passes to enter the construction site.

APPLICABLE LAWS, STANDARDS AND GUIDELINES
This section describes and aligns with national laws, international standards and Project-specific
guidance relevant to traffic and transport safety on the Rogun HPP construction site.
Tajikistan National Laws And Standards
Code Of Road Transport 2020 (Law No. 1689)
Governs vehicle operation, road usage, driver licensing, and road safety requirements. Measures
such as driver competency protocols, speed limits, and access controls outlined in the TMP must be
in accordance withthis law.
Construction Safety Regulations (GNIP PT 32-05-2015)
Approved by the Committee on Architecture and Construction, the GNIP PT 32-05-2015 regulations
establish safety standards for the construction of railway, road, and hydrotechnical tunnels. Specific
requirements relevant to the Rogun HPP include:
      Measures to segregate traffic and restrict pedestrian access to high-risk construction areas.
      Standards for operations in seismic zones, avalanche-prone regions, mudflow areas, and
       other difficult environments.
      Engineering measures and designs to protect land and underground structures during
       tunnelling activities, including stabilisation and structural integrity assessments.
      Requirements for the safe placement of equipment, efficient work scheduling, and
       operational safety during tunnel excavation.
Traffic and road safety measures addressing these project elements, as outlined in the TMP, must
comply with the GNIP PT 32-05-2015 regulations. Adherence to these standards is critical to
ensuring safe and legally compliant operations throughout the project’s lifecycle.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 186
Labor Code Of The Republic Of Tajikistan And The Law "On Labor Protection"
The TMP aligns with relevant national laws governing vehicle and equipment operations, ensuring
systematic risk assessment and safety management related to on-site traffic.
Risk management measures in the TMP, particularly in Section 3, address vehicle and equipment-
related hazards in accordance with national safety regulations.
Ministry Of Transport Regulations On Vehicle Inspection And Licensing
These regulations specify vehicle inspection and licensing procedures to maintain safety and
operational reliability. All vehicles used on-site must comply with these standards as part of the
TMP.
Law On Road Transport (Law No. 477)
This law establishes the legal framework for road transport operations in Tajikistan, defining
operator responsibilities, vehicle safety standards, and transport protocols. TMP measures must
comply with the following key provisions:
      Operator Responsibilities: Contractors must ensure that all vehicle operators hold valid
       licenses and meet national competency requirements.
      Vehicle Safety Standards: All vehicles operating on-site must meet national safety
       regulations, including required maintenance and inspection schedules.
      Traffic Protocols: Road use must follow established speed limits, overtaking restrictions,
       and vehicle hierarchy guidelines, ensuring safe interaction between light vehicles, heavy
       equipment, and pedestrians.
International Standards And Agreements
United Nations Economic Commission for Europe (UNECE) Transport Conventions
Tajikistan’s participation in UNECE Transport Conventions ensures that the TMP aligns with
international best practices for vehicle safety, operational protocols, and environmental risk
management. Specific requirements include:
      Vehicle and Machinery Safety: All vehicles and mobile equipment must comply with UNECE
       safety requirements, including rollover protection structures (ROPS), falling object protective
       structures (FOPS), and braking performance standards (refer to Sections 8, 9, and 10).
      Environmental Risk Management: Traffic-related risks such as landslides, rockfalls, and dust
       emissions must be managed in compliance with UNECE environmental safety standards
       (refer to Section 13).
International Environmental And Social Standards And Guidelines
World Bank ESF Standards
The TMP incorporates relevant World Bank Environmental and ESF standards to ensure effective
risk management, including:
ESS1: Assessment and Management of Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts:
Requires a systematic approach to identifying and mitigating traffic-related risks, including vehicle
emissions, noise pollution and accident prevention strategies.

ESS2: Labour and Working Conditions: Mandates strict vehicle operator competency standards,
ensuring compliance with national licensing and training requirements.
ESS3: Resource Efficiency and Pollution Prevention and Management: Ensures that traffic-

World Bank Guidelines And Notes
The following guidance documents supplement the ESF standards by offering detailed
recommendations for traffic safety and community health management:
Guidance Note for Borrowers: Environmental & Social Framework for IPF Operations – ESS3:
Resource Efficiency and Pollution Prevention and Management: Provides practical guidance for
minimizing environmental impacts from project-related traffic, including controlling vehicle emissions,
promoting fuel efficiency, and managing hazardous materials such as fuel and lubricants to prevent
spills and contamination.
Guidance Note for Borrowers: Environmental & Social Framework for IPF Operations – ESS4:
Community Health and Safety: Outlines practical guidance for integrating traffic safety measures
into project planning, particularly in high-risk areas near settlements or public roads.
General Environmental, Health, and Safety (EHS) Guidelines (2007): Section 3.0 – Community
Health and Safety: Covers best practices for road safety risk assessments, emergency response
planning and minimising vehicle-pedestrian interactions.
Lenders’ Guidelines and Standards
Asian Development Bank (ADB) Safeguard Policy Statement (SPS 2009) – Road Safety
      The ADB SPS 2009 requires road safety to be integrated into project planning, design, and
       implementation to minimise transport risks. This includes conducting risk assessments,
       enforcing speed management measures, ensuring proper road signage and infrastructure,
       addressing community safety concerns, and enforcing compliance among contractors and
       drivers.
      Road safety requirements under SPS 2009 are reflected in the TMP through structured risk-
       based traffic planning, contractor obligations, vehicle compliance measures, and clear
       enforcement of road safety controls across project transport routes.
Asian Development Bank (ADB) Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) (September
2024): Establishes traffic management as a key component of sustainable infrastructure projects
requiring site-wide controls for vehicle movement, safety training, and enforcement.
Institute of Environmental Management and Assessment (IEMA) Guidelines: Environmental
Assessment of Traffic and Movement (July 2023): Provides methodologies for assessing the
environmental impacts of traffic and movement, particularly related to emissions, congestion, and
public road interactions. These guidelines inform the assessment in Traffic and Transport Section of
this ESIA.

TRAFFIC RISK ASSESSMENT AND MITIGATION FRAMEWORK PLAN
Purpose and Scope
This section outlines the methodology and process undertaken to identify, evaluate, and address
traffic-related risks associated with on-site activities at the Rogun HPP. The assessment forms the
basis for the strategies and controls detailed in this TMP, ensuring that risks are effectively mitigated
to uphold safety, enhance operational efficiency, and ensure compliance with applicable standards.
In alignment with the World Bank Environmental and Social Standard 3 and 4 (ESS3 and ESS4),
this assessment utilised a multifaceted approach. This included a desktop analysis of Project
documents, a site traffic survey, and stakeholder consultations to assess current conditions, identify
discrepancies, gaps, potential risks, impacts and hazards and address site-specific traffic safety
challenges. While ESS4 primarily focuses on off-site road safety and community risks, its structured
approach to risk identification, evaluation, mitigation, and monitoring has informed this on-site Traffic
Management Plan (TMP). The principles of structured risk identification, evaluation, mitigation and
monitoring remain applicable in ensuring safe traffic management within the Project site. Moreover,
the assessment process was designed to align with international best practices for traffic
management, ensuring that mitigation measures support both safe on-site operations and
compliance with relevant global road safety standards.
Findings from the traffic assessment, combined with the review of the literature on industry
standards, best practices, and guidelines, informed the development of the mitigation measures and
control strategies and principles outlined in this TMP. These measures are tailored to the Project’s
unique and evolving conditions, ensuring alignment with established risk management principles,
WB ESF requirements, and the dynamic nature of the concurrent construction and operational
phases.
Traffic Assessment Methodology And Approach
Desktop Review And Gap Analysis Of Project Documentation
A comprehensive desktop review of contractor-submitted TMPs and related Project documentation
was conducted to evaluate existing traffic management practices and their alignment with applicable
standards. Key documents reviewed included:
      Traffic Management Plan for the Main Dam Construction (WeBuild, May 2024): Recently
       approved by the Employer’s Representative, this TMP served as a primary reference for
       assessing the existing documented traffic management controls formally deemed acceptable
       on-site.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                      October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                Page | 189
      Additional Contractor TMPs: These included Tunnel Sadd Ariana’s TMP for Lot 4 and
       TGEM’s Attachment 6 Traffic Assessment, submitted as part of their ESMP.
      Rogun JSC Security Department Documentation: Security regulations and job descriptions
       relevant to traffic and pedestrian safety were analysed to understand existing roles,
       responsibilities, and procedural frameworks.
      Traffic and Transport: Baseline data and mitigation measures outlined in this chapter
       informed the alignment of this TMP with the Project’s environmental and social (E&S)
       objectives.
The desktop review assessed existing documentation against applicable standards, including World
Bank ESF requirements, Tajikistan’s regulatory framework, and good international industry practices
(GIIP). This review informed the development of clear mitigation actions for the potential risks
identified by incorporating GIIP and making necessary adjustments where additional measures were
required.
Site Traffic Survey And Stakeholder Consultation

A site traffic survey was conducted at the Rogun HPP in November 2024 to evaluate on-the-ground
traffic conditions and practices. The survey encompassed site exploration across various
construction areas, contractor Lots, and critical infrastructure points to develop a comprehensive
understanding of site-wide activities. Key activities included:
      Observing vehicle movements, plant operations, and security protocols.
      Visiting tunnels, haul roads, and other high-traffic zones to document traffic flows and
       existing controls.
      Collaborating with the Employer’s Representative and Rogun JSC representatives to ensure
       thorough site access and operational insights.
      Documenting observations through notes and photographs to inform the TMP framework.
In addition, audits of occupational health and safety performance across the site in November 2023,
November 2024, and April 2025, included reviews of drivers’ licensing, inspections of vehicles and
equipment, and observations of driving and parking practices were conducted.
Consultations with key stakeholders on-site provided additional insights into existing practices and
operational challenges. These engagements included:
      Rogun JSC and the Employer’s Representative: To gain an understanding of traffic
       management objectives, operational constraints, procedural frameworks, and broader
       oversight challenges, including trends in driver behaviour and hazard and risk exposure
       associated with site conditions.
      Contractor Teams: Including We Build and subcontractors, to gather input on traffic
       management practices and site-specific operational conditions.
Alignment With World Bank ESF
The traffic assessment methodology followed structured risk assessment principles, incorporating
elements from the World Bank Environmental and Social Standard 4 (ESS3 and 4) where
applicable, as well as the Environmental and Social Framework for Investment Project Financing
(IPF) Operations - Good Practice Note: Road Safety. Key assessment components included:
      Site traffic surveys to evaluate road conditions, vehicle flow, and risk factors specific to
       construction and operational phases.

      Design reviews to assess road layouts, pedestrian safety provisions, and vehicle access
       controls.
      Stakeholder engagement with project personnel to address on-site safety challenges and
       contractor-specific traffic risks.
Key Traffic And Vehicle Movement Areas
Construction and operational activities at the Rogun HPP occur concurrently 24 hours per day, 7
days per week, involving continuous vehicle movements to support active construction, assembly,
and operational processes across various zones.
Key traffic and mobile plant operational areas include:
      Site access points
      Banks and inclines
      Aboveground access and haul roads
      Underground roads and tunnels
      Intersections and converging roadways
      Pedestrian and ground personnel activity
      Heavy mobile plant and equipment operations
      Manual traffic control points
      Parking and staging areas
Key Findings
This section presents an overview of key traffic-related risks and operational observations across
the project site, identified through a structured analysis using a 5x5 risk matrix. This approach
evaluates both the likelihood and consequence of potential traffic hazards ranging from pedestrian
safety and vehicle emissions to road degradation and hazardous material spillages. The findings are
based on a review of current Traffic Management Plans (TMPs) implemented on site, combined with
site visits, stakeholder consultations, and incident records. The matrix supports prioritization of
mitigation actions and informs the development of a harmonized, site-wide TMP framework.

The following traffic risks and hazards were identified during the traffic assessment process. This list
highlights critical areas requiring immediate attention to improve traffic safety, reduce risks, and
enhance operational efficiency across the site. While not exhaustive, it captures key findings that
inform the broader traffic management strategy.
The chart below presents a visual synthesis of key traffic-related risks identified across the Rogun
Hydropower Project site, based on site inspections, incident reports, and observations of existing
Traffic Management Plan (TMP) practices. Each category reflects recurring safety concerns,
operational weaknesses, or compliance gaps that require corrective actions. The frequency of
observations per category highlights priority areas for risk mitigation most notably infrastructure
deficiencies, unsafe driving behaviors, and inadequate vehicle safety systems, emphasizing the
need for an integrated, site-wide approach to traffic management and control.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 192
Drawing on site observations and a review of current practices, this analysis highlights key
vulnerabilities and operational gaps that require immediate and sustained attention within the Traffic
Management Plan :
Vehicle-Pedestrian Interactions
High-risk zones were identified where vehicle and pedestrian movements were not adequately
segregated or controlled, including the main site entrance gate, the dam core construction area, as
well as many underground roads through tunnels.
Workers were observed crossing active vehicle paths in unmarked areas, while vehicles stopped in
unsafe locations such as intersections and tunnels.
Driver Behaviour and Traffic Discipline
Many instances of unsafe driving practices, such as speeding, overtaking in restricted zones, and
using mobile phones while operating vehicles, were identified during the assessment.
Non-compliance with traffic controls, including ignoring signals and stop signs, was prevalent.
Additionally, many vehicles were observed operating without functioning seatbelts, or drivers failed
to use them, compromising occupant safety.
Workers in tunnels were frequently observed without high-visibility clothing, significantly increasing
the risk of vehicle-pedestrian collisions in low-light and confined conditions.
Traffic Signalling and Congestion

Manual flagging operations in tunnels were inconsistent, sometimes attentive to traffic and
sometimes not.
Manual flagging operations in tunnels were assessed as high-risk due to low visibility, hazardous
fumes, and insufficient segregation.


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 193
Traffic congestion during peak periods, such as shift changes, was reported as a contributing factor
to increased accident risks.
Infrastructure Deficiencies

Key high-traffic zones, including intersections and the main haul road convergence point for heavy
machinery and contractor vehicles, lacked adequate signage and flagging. Limited visibility due to
vegetation, road gradients, and obstructed sightlines on ramps and slopes heightened the risk of
collisions.
Narrow roads and steep inclines without barriers, such as concrete blocks or berms, posed
significant risks of vehicles overturning or veering off-road and falling.
Poor drainage, potholes, and unmaintained surfaces contributed to hazardous driving conditions,
including skidding and reduced vehicle control.
Insufficient lighting and the absence of reflective markers in high-risk areas, such as some tunnels
and sharp bends.
Environmental Hazards

Landslides and rockfalls were identified as potential risks in geologically unstable areas.
Heavy rainfall. poor drainage systems and de-watering processes caused water pooling, increasing
risks of skidding and vehicle instability.
Snow-fall and Haze were also identified as weather induced hazards that can impede visibility and
make the routes slippery.
Vehicle Safety Systems and Communication Practices
Many vehicles operated without identification markers, functioning reversing alarms, or lights.
Communication devices, such as two-way radios, were not implemented or underutilised, leading to
reliance on ineffective alternatives like use of vehicle horn, or no positive communication when
overtaking vehicles, such as heavy haul trucks in tunnels.
Vehicles did not have markings that would allow identification of the owner and operator from a
distance.
Many vehicles did not have charged fire extinguishers or working gauges, and some had cracked or
broken windshields or windows.
Unsafe Worker Drop-Off and Pick-Up Practices

Shuttle buses and worker transport vehicles were observed stopping in hazardous locations,
including intersections and tunnels, creating risks for both pedestrians and vehicles.
The absence of designated, signed, or segregated safe zones for bus stops heightened the
likelihood of incidents during worker movements.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                        October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                  Page | 194
Driver Licensing
Many drivers did not have proof they were authorized to operate the vehicles and equipment they
were driving/operating. Some heavy equipment operators had only licenses to operate passenger
vehicles in their home countries.
Induction, Training, and Awareness

There are site-wide induction programs and traffic awareness campaigns, but they have not been
effective, given the observed traffic practices on the site.
Monitoring and Inspection
Insufficient oversight and monitoring of traffic compliance allows persistent violations, including
unsafe worker transport and speeding.
Inconsistent enforcement of site-wide traffic rules, such as speed limits and pedestrian controls,
contributes to non-compliance and increased safety risks
Documentation Review And Compliance Inspection Of Existing Contractor TMPS
The existing Contractor TMPs were reviewed and found to include generally appropriate
requirements, although they were somewhat uneven, not necessarily consistent, and in some cases
incomplete. An important point is that each of the Contractor’s TMP, tend to focus on their
respective Lots, which points to the need for a clear and consistent delineation of site-wide
requirements, harmonization and coordination.
Observations on site also made it clear there was insufficient management oversight and
enforcement of existing traffic rules.
Summary
The assessment of traffic management at the Rogun HPP highlighted significant challenges,
including safety risks, operational inefficiencies, and systemic gaps in traffic controls, practices, and
documentation. These issues underscore the need for a cohesive, site-wide approach to address
the dynamic and high-risk activities during construction and operational phases of the project.
Key findings revealed misalignment between documented TMPs and on-site practices, insufficient
integration of contractor TMPs, and inadequate monitoring and enforcement mechanisms. These
gaps necessitate a comprehensive traffic management framework to ensure alignment with project
safety objectives, regulatory requirements, and evolving site conditions.
The subsequent sections of this TMP present a detailed site-wide traffic management approach,
principles and corresponding albeit appropriate hazard mitigation measures. These mitigation
measures are designed to address the identified challenges, risks, gaps, enhance traffic safety,
improve operational efficiency, and support the successful implementation of the project’s goals in a
manner that is consistent with the WB ESF, Tajikistan’s national laws and GIIP.
Traffic Risk Management Plan Framework
Duty Of Care

This TMP is developed in accordance with the principle that all duty holders, including Rogun JSC,
The Employers Representative, the PMC, contractors, and site security personnel, must, so far as is
reasonably practicable, ensure the health and safety of workers engaged, influenced, or directed by


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                       October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                 Page | 195
their work activities. This responsibility extends to protecting workers, contractors, visitors, and the
public from risks associated with on-site traffic and transport activities.
Alignment With Tajikistan Legislation

The TMP aligns with the provisions of the Labor Code of the Republic of Tajikistan and the Law of
the Republic of Tajikistan "On Labor Protection” as they relate to traffic safety and vehicle operations
in the workplace. These laws establish the legal framework for risk assessment and hazard control
in transport-related activities, ensuring that vehicle operation, traffic management, and worker safety
protocols are systematically evaluated and enforced.
Additionally, findings from recent Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) audits have informed this
TMP, particularly regarding identified risks associated with vehicle-pedestrian interactions,
compliance with seatbelt and speed regulations, and the adequacy of traffic control measures in
high-risk areas. These insights have been incorporated into site-wide traffic risk management
strategies to ensure regulatory compliance and enhance safety across the project.
Risk Assessment and Alternative Traffic Management Controls
This section establishes the minimum technical standards for on-site traffic management. The EPC
and “early works” Contractors must:
      Conduct Lot-specific risk assessments and implement additional control measures where
       needed.
      Determine appropriate locations for traffic controls, flaggers, signage, and training
       requirements based on their operational risks.
      Ensure all traffic management measures are aligned with site-wide safety protocols unless
       they provide adequate justification for alterations or deviations.
Smaller contractors may comply with the site-wide TMP rather than developing their own TMPs. If
they wish to deviate from the site-wide TMP in any way, they must:
      Propose alternative risk controls for review and approval by the ER/PMC.
      Justify such alternatives with a risk assessment .
EPC and “early works” Contractors must submit their TMPs aligned with this site-wide TMP within
30 days of its effective date, with full approval by the ER/PMC and implementation required no later
than 90 days.
The Contractors’ TMPs must be reviewed at least annually to reflect changes in site conditions,
construction progress, operational adjustments, and emerging traffic risks. All updates are subject to
review and approval by the ER/PMC to maintain compliance with project objectives, safety
protocols, and industry best practices. The site-wide TMP will be reviewed by the ER/PMC at least
annually and updated as needed.
 The ER/PMC will oversee contractor adherence to this TMP, ensuring proactive risk management
through pre-operation inspections, routine maintenance, and real-time hazard monitoring,
maintaining consistent site-wide traffic safety standards based on best industry practices, and
enforcing corrective actions when safety violations or traffic hazards are identified.
Risk Management Principles
Key principles of the TMP's framework include:


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                       October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                 Page | 196
      Acknowledging Hazards: Recognising all road traffic interactions as potential hazards,
       including those involving heavy equipment, passenger transport, and pedestrian crossings.
      Prioritising Systemic Measures: Applying controls that do not rely solely on individual
       behaviour, such as segregating traffic routes, implementing automated safety systems, and
       enforcing clear traffic rules.
      Minimising Residual Risks: Addressing residual risks through a structured application of
       the risk mitigation hierarchy and controls, with continuous assessments to adapt to evolving
       site conditions.
      Ensuring Communication and Awareness: Making sure that all parties responsible for
       traffic safety—including Rogun JSC, the Employer’s Representative, the Project
       Management Consultant (PMC), contractors, and site security—are fully aware of their roles
       and responsibilities. Regular coordination meetings, briefings, and training must reinforce a
       shared understanding of site-wide traffic management objectives.
      Adaptable and Relevant: Flexibility to accommodate changing site conditions and
       operational needs while maintaining alignment with the health, safety, and efficiency goals of
       the Rogun HPP Project.
      Documented and Updated: TMP measures must be clearly documented and regularly
       reviewed and updated to incorporate changes in site conditions, construction progress, or
       emerging risks, with a view to ensuring their ongoing effectiveness and practicality.
As Low As Reasonably Practicable (ALARP) Approach

The TMP adopts the ALARP principle, emphasising the balance between the level of risk and the
effort, time, and cost required to mitigate it. This ensures that risks associated with road traffic are
systematically minimised to acceptable levels.
Key Considerations in the ALARP Approach
      Likelihood and Consequences: Assessing the probability of hazards and their potential
       impacts.
      Degree of Harm: Evaluating the severity of potential harm resulting from identified risks.
      Knowledge and Control Options: Applying the best available methods to eliminate or reduce
       risks.
Site-Wide Consultation And Collaboration
A collaborative risk assessment process is critical to the successful implementation of TMP
measures. This process ensures that risk management strategies are informed by comprehensive
evaluations of site hazards and stakeholder insights. It involves:
      Operational Input: Contractor managers provide critical insights from daily operations,
       identifying specific risks and practical challenges within their areas of responsibility.
      Strategic Oversight: Rogun JSC and the ER/PMC ensure that risk assessments account for
       Project-wide impacts, align with safety standards, and comply with regulatory requirements.
      Stakeholder Engagement: Contributions from all relevant stakeholders help identify potential
       gaps in controls and address practical challenges in implementing effective safety measures.
Risk Mitigation Hierarchy

This Traffic risk assessment and management plan will apply a mitigation hierarchy which will:
      Anticipate and avoid risks and impacts;


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                       October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                 Page | 197
      Where avoidance is not possible, minimize or reduce risks and impacts to acceptable levels;
      Once risks and impacts have been minimized or reduced, mitigate; and
      Where significant residual impacts remain, compensate for or offset them, where technically
       and financially feasible.
Hierarchy Of Control
The hierarchy of control provides a structured approach to mitigating traffic hazards, prioritising
measures that deliver the highest levels of protection and reliability. This systematic method ensures
that risks associated with road traffic are minimised to a level that is ALARP. This framework is
designed to reduce risks for all personnel operating within or moving through the project site,
including workers, contractors, and authorised visitors.
Application of the Hierarchy of Control
The TMP addresses all road traffic exposure as a potential hazard, applying the following principles
to eliminate, substitute, isolate, or reduce risks through systemic measures:
      Elimination: Remove the hazard entirely by reducing unnecessary vehicle movements,
       optimising material deliveries, and eliminating redundant transport activities. While
       elimination is the most effective control, practical constraints, such as the need for vehicle
       operations during construction, may limit feasibility.
      Substitution: Replace hazardous activities with safer alternatives. For example, consolidating
       worker transport into shared vehicles reduces individual vehicle movements and congestion
       risks.
      Engineering Controls: Implement physical and systemic changes to the work environment to
       separate workers from hazards. Examples include installing barriers to protect pedestrians,
       segregating traffic routes, and upgrading road infrastructure with barriers, signage, lighting,
       and reflective markers as needed to improve safety and efficiency.
      Administrative Controls: Develop and enforce policies and procedures to regulate traffic
       activities. Scheduling vehicle movements during off-peak times, providing robust training and
       induction programs, and implementing clear traffic rules are essential for maintaining
       discipline and compliance.
      Personal Protective Equipment (PPE): PPE remains vital for mitigating residual risks. As
       examples, workers in traffic zones and in tunnels must use high-visibility clothing and
       appropriate safety gear and all drivers and passengers must consistently use safety belts.
Traffic Management Plan Implementation
The findings from the traffic assessment inform the phased implementation of control measures.
This approach prioritises immediate risk mitigation while creating a roadmap for long-term
improvements. High-priority measures are addressed in initial phases, followed by comprehensive
infrastructure upgrades and systemic controls.
The phased implementation strategy, including timelines, responsibilities, and recommendations, is
detailed in Section 17 and supported by the Phased Implementation Roadmap. This ensures that
the TMP evolves in tandem with the Project’s dynamic construction and operational requirements,
delivering a cohesive and adaptive traffic management framework.

VEHICLE AND MOBILE PLANT STANDARDS
Vehicle And Mobile Plant Types
The Rogun HPP Project employs a variety of vehicles and mobile equipment to support
construction, logistics, and operational activities. These are categorised based on their frequency of
use and functional roles on-site.
Frequent Use Vehicles
Essential for daily operations, these vehicles transport personnel, materials, and supplies, primarily
along designated access routes and logistical corridors:
      Shuttle buses
      Cars/light vehicles (sedans and four-wheel-drive trucks for worker transportation and general
       transport)
      Dumper trucks
      Cement mixer trucks
      Fuel trucks
      Water trucks
Core Site Vehicles and Heavy Mobile Plant
Specialised machinery supporting high-impact construction tasks within restricted zones, such as
the HPP construction site, includes:
      Bulldozers
      Roller compactors
      Excavators
      Mobile cranes
      Drilling machines
These vehicles will be subject to strict operational controls due to their size and function and
generally remain within assigned construction areas.
Mixed-Use and Auxiliary Equipment

Supporting a range of construction and maintenance activities, these vehicles operate across
shared and restricted zones as required:
      Forklifts
      Light utility vehicles
      Maintenance trucks
Site-Wide Integration
The standards and controls outlined in this TMP apply to all types of vehicles and mobile plant,
ensuring consistent site-wide compliance with traffic management protocols, safe coordination of
movements across mixed-use zones, and effective mitigation of risks associated with high-traffic
areas.

Vehicle And Mobile Plant Selection, Suitability, and Pre-Inspection Requirements
To ensure safe, efficient operations and mitigate potential risks, all vehicles and mobile equipment
deployed on-site must comply with the following minimum requirements for selection, suitability, and
pre-inspection.
Site Entry: Risk Assessment And Approval Process
All vehicles and mobile plant must undergo a formal documented evaluation by the Contractor or by
the ER/PMC before being brought to site. This process ensures compliance with site-specific safety
and operational standards. The contractor is responsible for ensuring the unit is in a safe,
roadworthy condition and equipped for on-site tasks.
The evaluation focuses on identifying any potential safety risks or deficiencies that could
compromise the unit’s performance or pose hazards to personnel and equipment. This pre-entry
certification process is critical to maintaining site safety and ensuring vehicles and mobile plant meet
regulatory and project-specific requirements.
The assessment records must be submitted to the ER/PMC for review and approval prior to site
entry. Vehicles or equipment that fail to meet these standards will not be permitted on-site until
necessary repairs or adjustments are completed and the unit is re-evaluated. Compliance will be
assessed against fit-for-purpose and equipment safety criteria outlined in the formal pre-site
evaluation assessment form, which includes verification of mechanical condition, maintenance
records, and key safety features. These requirements must align with the safety device and vehicle
condition criteria detailed in Sections 8.2.4, 8.3, and 8.4 of this framework TMP.
Suitability For Task
Vehicles and mobile equipment must be suitable for their assigned roles, ensuring safe and effective
operation in line with site conditions and task requirements.
Minimum suitability criteria include:
       Equipment must match the weight, and volume demands of assigned tasks to prevent
        overloading and ensure safe operation.
       Vehicles and equipment must be capable of navigating site layouts, including tight or
        restricted areas, with ease and stability.
       Equipment must be suitable for operation on variable site terrain, including inclined, rough, or
        unpaved surfaces typical of the Rogun HPP site.
Compliance With Operational Standards

All vehicles and mobile equipment must meet operational standards established in this site wide
framework TMP to ensure safe, efficient, and compliant use on-site
Key requirements include:
       Manufacturer Guidelines: Vehicles and equipment must operate according to manufacturer
        instructions. Modifications affecting safety or integrity are prohibited unless explicitly
        approved by the ER or PMC, with supporting safety documentation.
       Operation and Maintenance Compliance: Adhere to O&M manuals for handling
        procedures, load limits, and safe operation in rugged site conditions like Rogun HPP.

      Load Security: Secure materials and equipment using industry-standard load-securing
       techniques. Verify load securing, loose items, and balance during pre-operation inspections.
      Conformance to Site Protocols: Align with this site-wide TMP, contractor-specific TMPs,

      Where non-compliance is identified, the Contactor/ER/PMC or the Traffic Safety Section will

Maintenance And Inspection Requirements
Daily And Pre-Shift Inspections
All vehicles and mobile equipment must undergo daily and pre-shift inspections to verify operational
safety and compliance with site requirements, as required by the Project’s OHS requirements.
Operators must complete these inspections before use, utilising an approved checklist.
The Traffic Department is responsible for maintaining an inventory of all vehicles, including
identification numbers. Gate staff must verify compliance before allowing site entry, and for
registering visitors’ vehicles.
The following safety-critical components must be checked during each inspection:
      Braking System: Service brakes, emergency brakes, and ABS (if applicable) must be
       functional.
      Steering Mechanism: Full operability, with no excessive play or defects.
      Tyres and Wheels: Adequate tread depth, proper inflation, and no excessive wear.
      Lights and Signals: Headlights, brake lights, turn signals, hazard lights, and reversing lights
       must be operational.
      Mirrors and Visibility: Windshields, side windows, and mirrors must be intact and clean for
       clear visibility.
      Audible Warning Systems: Horn and reversing alarms must be functional.
      Seatbelts: Fully operational seatbelts for all seating positions—in use by drivers and
       passengers.
      Glass. Windows and windshield must be intact, with no cracks or holes.
      Emergency Equipment: Fire extinguisher (securely mounted), first aid kit, spill containment
       supplies, and basic spare parts (e.g., fuses, bulbs).
      Identifier Placard. A sign/placard with a distinct identifying number /letter combination will
       be visible on the front, rear, and sides of all vehicles and mobile plant.

Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025

A completed “pre-start checklist” must be kept in the vehicle or equipment. Any vehicle or equipment
released from a workshop or maintenance facility must undergo a post-maintenance inspection, with
a corresponding record signed by the maintenance supervisor before returning to operation.
Contractor supervisors must verify completed inspection records daily to ensure compliance. The
Traffic Department and Rogun JSC may conduct random audits to verify adherence and identify any
systemic failures in the inspection process.
Mandatory Safety Devices And Equipment
All site vehicles and mobile equipment must be equipped with safety features to reduce risks of
collisions, pedestrian interactions, infrastructure damage, rollovers, and operational hazards. These
safety features must be regularly inspected and maintained in full working order.
The following safety features must be installed and maintained in all site vehicles and equipment,
with applicability determined by vehicle type, operational use, and site-specific conditions:
      Seatbelts: Functional seatbelts are required for all seating positions. Shuttle buses, delivery
       trucks, and passenger vehicles must have three-point seatbelts for each seat. Transporting
       passengers outside of designated seating areas is strictly prohibited.
      Audible Alarms and Visual Indicators: Reverse alarms and flashing beacons must
       activate automatically when reversing or conducting other high-risk manoeuvres.
      Two-Way Communication Devices: Radios or equivalent communication devices must be
       installed for coordination, particularly for overtaking, passing, and high-traffic operations.
      Lighting and Signals: Operational headlights, brake lights, turn signals, hazard lights, and
       reversing lights are mandatory. For tunnel operations, vehicles must be fitted with high-
       intensity auxiliary lights to ensure adequate visibility in low-light environments. These must
       meet minimum lumens output and positioning standards as determined by the Traffic
       Department.
      Braking and Stability Systems: ABS must be installed on all heavy vehicles where
       practicable, considering existing fleet configurations. Machinery operating on slopes must
       have stability control systems and outriggers to prevent tipping.
      Fire & Spill Control Equipment: All vehicles must carry a fire extinguisher, first aid kit, spill
       containment supplies, and basic spare parts (e.g., bulbs, fuses) for minor repairs.
      Protective Structures & Enclosures: Existing ROPS must be maintained on applicable
       machinery such as bulldozers, loaders, and excavators. New equipment purchases should
       include ROPS where feasible. Heavy equipment must have enclosed cabs with air filtration
       systems to reduce dust exposure.
      Vehicle Identification & Safety Markings: All vehicles must display unique identification
       numbers and contractor names, clearly visible from the front, rear, and sides. Identification
       numbers must be no more than five characters and readable from at least 25 metres in all
       weather conditions. Reflective materials must be used, particularly for vehicles operating in
       low-light environments such as tunnels.
      Anti-Collision Systems : Vehicles and heavy equipment should include sensors and alerts
       to reduce accident risks in high-traffic or low-visibility areas where feasible. This is
       recommended but not required, given the existing fleet and site conditions.

COMPLIANCE AND MONITORING
The Traffic Department must maintain a central inventory of all project vehicles and equipment,
ensuring compliance with identification and safety feature requirements, while the Security Team at
the main gate must verify vehicle compliance before allowing entry.
The ER/PMC must conduct routine inspections to confirm that all vehicles meet safety requirements,
and all vehicles must be regularly cleaned and maintained to ensure that safety markings and
features remain fully functional.
The placards with identification numbers/letters will allow the Traffic Department, the ER/PMC,
Contractors, and other parties to identify and report vehicles observed to be violating traffic
standard. A central inventory will allow the ER/PMC and/or Traffic Department to notify the vehicle’s
owner/operator and require corrective action.
Vehicle Identification Requirements

As mentioned above, all construction and operational vehicles must display a unique identifier
prominently visible on the front, rear, and both sides of the vehicle. The ER/PMC and the Traffic
Department will determine the nature of he identifier, which will likely be a number/letter
combination, possibly with the owner’s name also displayed.
The identifier must:
      Have minimum dimensions of 300 mm (height) × 150 mm (width) on the front and rear, and
       200 mm (height) × 100 mm (width) on both sides.
      Be retrofitted onto all existing site vehicles within 60 days of the TMP’s approval.
The Employer’s Representative and/or Rogun JSC’s Traffic or Safety Department will conduct
random spot checks to verify compliance with vehicle identification requirements. Contractors must
ensure that:
      Identifiers remain clearly visible at all times, free from dirt, damage, or obstructions.
      Routine cleaning and maintenance of identification markings is performed to uphold visibility
       standards.
      Any faded, damaged, or missing markings are promptly restored upon notification or
       observation.
All vehicles operating on-site, including those owned or used by Rogun JSC, contractors, and
visiting organisations (e.g., PMG, DFZ, World Bank representatives), must comply with vehicle
identification requirements.
      Vehicles must display approved identification markings before being granted entry to the site.
      Occasional or visiting vehicles must obtain a temporary vehicle permit issued by Rogun JSC
       at designated offices before arrival or, if necessary, at the site entrance.
      Gate guards must verify vehicle identification, permits, and driver credentials before allowing
       access, in line with existing site security and ID/passport checks.
General Operational Safety Requirements
Operational safety protocols define the minimum requirements for the safe use of vehicles and
mobile equipment on-site. These measures aim to protect operators, ground personnel, and
infrastructure while mitigating risks associated with construction activities.

Operational Boundaries And Segregation Controls
To enhance site traffic safety and minimise interaction between vehicles, equipment, and personnel,
all Contractors must assess, define, and implement operational boundaries and segregation
controls. The following segregation and boundary controls are mandatory and must be identified,
marked, and maintained by Contractors within their areas of operation. All of these measures must
be described in the respective Contractors’ TMPs. The ER/PMC will be responsible for areas that
are under Rogun JSC control.
Contractors must install and maintain physical barriers at high-risk locations, including:
      Concrete barriers, guardrails, or fencing to separate heavy equipment operations from
       general work areas.
      Slope protection barriers (e.g., berms, reinforced guardrails) to prevent vehicle rollovers and
       protect workers in unstable terrain. Caution tape will not be acceptable.
      Delineators, cones, or bollards to segregate traffic and control movement.
      Barrier locations must be identified and inspected regularly for integrity.
Contractors must install and maintain signage and road markings at key locations, covering:
      Speed Limits – Clearly marked and enforced for all vehicle types.
      Restricted and Danger Areas – Marking high-risk zones, excavation areas, and tunnel
       entrances.
      Right-of-Way and Yield Zones – Indicating vehicle priority at intersections and merging
       points.
      Load Restrictions – Posting weight and clearance limits for bridges, tunnels, and haul roads.
      Traffic Flow Indicators – Marking one-way routes, pedestrian crossings (where authorised),
       and stop zones.
      All signage must be reflective and visible in low-light conditions. Contractors must ensure
       markings are maintained and repainted as necessary
Pedestrian access is prohibited in high-risk areas unless explicitly authorised and controlled. This
includes:
      Haul roads, heavy equipment zones, tunnels, and excavation sites.
Where pedestrian access is necessary, Contractors must:
      Define and mark designated pedestrian walkways.
      Install physical separation barriers (e.g., fencing, barricades).
      Clearly mark pedestrian crossings and enforce controlled movement zones.
      Ensure pedestrians are wearing high-visibility clothing/vests.
Contractors must document pedestrian restrictions.
Where required, Contractors must assign trained personnel to control traffic in high-risk areas,
including:
      Traffic Controllers - Managing flow at congested intersections.
      Banksmen - Directing heavy equipment in confined areas.



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                       October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                 Page | 204
      Flaggers - Assisting with temporary traffic diversions.
All traffic control personnel must use radio communication, or in areas where this isn’t viable (e.g.
tunnels) use alternative communication methods such as designated signallers or hardwired
communication systems, and wear high-visibility PPE.
Contractors must assess and define segregation controls including:
      Barriers, signage, pedestrian restrictions, and traffic controllers.
      Site-specific hazard identification and required control measures.
      Methods for maintaining, updating, and enforcing segregation measures.
The Employer’s Representative / PMC will verify compliance through regular inspections and audits.
In high-risk zones like the dam core, where concurrent operations occur, strict adherence to
segregation controls and operational boundaries is essential to prevent overlap between personnel
and machinery. Regular monitoring and adjustment of these boundaries is essential to support safe,
coordinated movements, during multi-activity operations.
Shutdown And Securing Procedures
When not in use, all equipment must be fully powered down, brakes engaged, and attachments
such as blades or booms grounded. The key must always be removed when the operator or driver is
not in the cab to prevent unauthorised use.
Fuelling And Lubrication Protocols
Fuelling and lubrication activities must occur in designated zones, adhering to the following
guidelines:
Maintain a minimum 20 m distance from active operations.
Implement spill containment measures (e.g., operate only over spill trays, ensure spill kit is
available, etc.) to mitigate environmental risks.
Follow fire safety protocols, including prohibitions on open flames.
Safe Operating Procedures (SOPS)
Contractors must develop Standard Operation Procedures (SOPs) for each equipment type based
on site-specific risk assessments and manufacturer guidelines. SOPs should:
      Define safe handling practices and operational limits.
      Specify activity-specific risk controls.
      Provide clear instructions on hazard mitigation and operational safety for equipment
       operators.
      Define qualifications and training requirements for driver/operators and issue licenses that
       identify the vehicle/equipment type the person is authorized to drive/operate.
Standards For Oversized And Complex Loads
All oversized and abnormal loads transported on-site must comply with the following planning
control and safety requirements. These measures are necessary to prevent incidents, minimise
disruption and ensure the safe movement of large or complex loads within the project area. For
detailed protocols related to off-site transport, refer to the framework OS-TMP.


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 205
Route Planning And Risk Assessment
Before any oversized or complex load is transported, a route plan and risk assessment must be
conducted to identify site-specific constraints, restricted areas, and potential conflict points. The
assessment must include an evaluation of narrow passages, steep inclines, low-clearance zones,
and intersections where traffic conflicts may arise. Areas with restricted access must be clearly
identified, and necessary authorisations must be obtained before transportation proceeds. Risk
assessments must be documented and submitted to the PMC for review before transport operations
begin. In addition, prior notice must be issued to the ER/PMC and Security Department to
coordinate safe movement of oversized loads within the site.
Escort And Warning Measures
All oversized loads must be escorted by designated safety vehicles to ensure safe transit through
high-risk areas. Vehicles transporting oversized loads must display warning signage on both the
front and rear to alert other road users. Where manoeuvring space is limited, or interactions with
standard site traffic create hazards, temporary traffic controls must be implemented. These
measures may include road closures, the deployment of flaggers, or restricted access to certain
zones. Contractors must coordinate load movements in advance with the PMC/ER and the Traffic
Safety Section to prevent disruptions to ongoing site operations.
Load Securement

All loads must be secured using industry-standard securement techniques. This includes the use of
appropriate tie-downs, bracing, and stabilisation devices to prevent shifting during transit. Load
stability and securement devices must be inspected before transport, at periodic intervals during
transit, and upon arrival at the designated location. Any deficiencies identified during inspections
must be rectified immediately before transportation can continue.
Heavy Equipment And Mobile Plant: Operational Requirements And Safety Controls
Heavy equipment and mobile plant play a critical role in high-impact construction activities at Rogun
HPP. These machines require stringent operational protocols and safety measures to mitigate risks
associated with their size, weight, and complexity.
Minimum Requirements
The following are the minimum expected controls for operating key types of plant on-site. These
requirements are supplementary to the general operational requirements outlined in Section 8.5 and
the mandatory safety devices and equipment detailed in Section 8.4.
Contractors must conduct task-specific risk assessments for all equipment types and implement
additional controls where necessary to ensure safe work and operating practices. These
assessments must be documented and submitted to the PMC for review as part of ongoing safety
management.
Contractors must ensure the following minimum requirements for each equipment type:
      Excavators
      Conduct daily inspections of hydraulic systems, hoses, and stability controls before
       operation.

      Operate exclusively within designated zones, ensuring no personnel are present in the swing
       radius.
      Avoid steep descents; maintain slow, controlled movements, and ground booms when
       stationary.
      Bulldozers
      Limit operations to slopes ≤ 30° and engage stability controls to prevent tipping.
      Avoid sudden directional changes, particularly on gradients or embankments.
      Ground blades when idle and refrain from sharp turns on slopes to minimise tipping risks.
      Loaders and Mobile Cranes
       o   Adhere to load limits and ensure clearance near embankments, high-traffic areas, and
           restricted zones.
       o   Maintain clear communication between operators and ground personnel to coordinate
           safe material delivery and equipment movements.
       o   Conduct daily inspections, focusing on load stability and hoisting mechanisms.
      Dump Trucks and Water Trucks
       o   Operate strictly within designated routes to prevent congestion and unauthorised access
           to restricted zones.
       o   Ensure load distribution complies with manufacturer specifications and site-specific
           requirements to maintain vehicle stability.
       o   Regularly inspect tank and body integrity, ensuring no leaks or loose fittings for water
           trucks, and secure tailgates for dump trucks to prevent spillage during transit.
      Concrete Pumps and Mixers
       o   Operate only on stable, level ground to prevent tipping or structural stress, and ensure
           the work area is clear of obstructions.
       o   Strictly adhere to manufacturer-specified load, pressure, and operational capacity limits.
       o   Inspect hydraulic systems, hoses, safety devices, and pump mechanisms before each
           use to confirm proper functioning and identify wear or damage.
       o   Ensure all safety guards and emergency shutoff controls are operational and accessible
           during use.
Loading, Unloading, And Lifting Equipment Trucks

Loading, unloading, and lifting operations on-site require adherence to specific safety protocols to
ensure the security of personnel, vehicles, and equipment. Minimum requirements include, but are
not limited to:
      Proper Lifting Equipment: Use cranes, forklifts, and other lifting equipment suitable for the
       material's weight and size. Inspect equipment daily, operate within manufacturer load limits,
       and secure all load-bearing attachments.
      Stability and Clearance: Confirm vehicles are stable on level ground before operations. Use
       outriggers and stabilisers as needed, especially on uneven or inclined surfaces.
      Traffic and Access Controls: Establish temporary traffic controls (e.g., barriers, signage) to
       restrict unauthorised access. Contractors must manage traffic flow in these zones to ensure
       safety.
