ENVIRONMENTAL TRAFFIC HAZARD MITIGATION
PRIMARY ENVIRONMENTAL HAZARDS ON SITE
Numerous natural and environmental hazards present on the Rogun HPP site pose unique risks to
drivers, pedestrians, and site infrastructure.
Key hazards identified include, but are not limited to:
      Adverse weather conditions, including heavy rainfall, snowfall, and temperature fluctuations,
       resulting in wet and icy road surfaces, reduced visibility, and increased risks of rockfalls and
       landslides.
      Rockfalls along high-elevation and exposed roadways
      Landslides and unstable ground conditions in mountainous terrain
      Flooding and water accumulation in tunnels and core construction zones during heavy
       rainfall
      Wildlife intrusions, particularly cattle and stray dogs, creating hazards on site roads and
       access paths
These conditions can obstruct traffic, damage infrastructure, and, critically, endanger vehicle
operators and ground personnel. Effective mitigation, monitoring, and response protocols are
essential to maintain safety, minimise incident risks, and ensure site accessibility throughout the
project.
ROCKFALL AND LANDSLIDE MANAGEMENT
        Rockfalls and landslides pose significant risks due to the mountainous terrain, high
elevations, and ongoing construction at the Rogun HPP. These hazards are particularly critical along
dam haul roads, tunnel access points, and within tunnels. Traffic management must integrate with
site-wide rockfall and landslide controls to ensure vehicle and pedestrian safety.
The Employer’s Representative and PMC, in coordination with contractors, must establish
monitoring, hazard response, and mitigation measures at high-risk locations, which must be
incorporated into Contractor TMPs. Key traffic-related controls include:




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 228
      Road and Tunnel Inspections: Contractors must conduct regular inspections of roads and
       tunnel entrances, particularly after adverse weather or blasting activities, and remove loose
       debris to maintain safe transit routes.
      Protective Infrastructure: Where necessary, barriers, mesh installations, or stabilisation
       structures must be installed to mitigate rockfall risks along vehicle routes.
      Emergency Response and Road Closures: In the event of a rockfall or landslide, affected
       roads must be closed immediately, with alternative routes communicated to all site personnel
       through the established emergency notification system.
TUNNEL-SPECIFIC ROCKFALL PRECAUTIONS
Specific measures are required to mitigate tunnel-related rockfall risks:
      Stabilisation of Tunnel Roofs and Walls: Conduct regular assessments of tunnel roofs and
       walls to identify loose rock formations. Apply stabilisation methods such as rock bolting,
       shotcrete, and mesh installations where necessary.
      Real-Time Monitoring: Employ real-time monitoring systems in high-risk tunnels to detect
       early signs of instability. Contractor personnel must be trained to respond promptly to alerts,
       including evacuation procedures.
MACHINERY AND EQUIPMENT STANDARDS
All equipment used in high-risk areas must meet specific safety standards:
      ROPS and FOPS: Machinery operating in rockfall-prone areas must be equipped with
       Rollover Protective Structures (ROPS) and Falling Object Protective Structures (FOPS) to
       safeguard operators.
      Load Securing: Equipment used for material handling must be equipped to securely fasten
       loads, using approved tie-downs, nets, or barriers to prevent debris from dislodging or falling
       into transit areas
FLOOD AND WATER MANAGEMENT IN TUNNELS AND CORE AREAS
WATER ACCUMULATION AND DRAINAGE REQUIREMENTS
Water management in tunnels and core areas may be needed at times and locations where it
presents a safety risk to traffic operations. The ER/PMC and Contractors must assess whether
water accumulation is an issue in tunnels. Where water accumulation is identified as a risk,
contractors must integrate drainage and water control measures into their TMPs. Requirements may
include maintaining functional drainage systems, conducting routine inspections, rapid water
removal to prevent vehicle hazards, or temporary road closures.


EMERGENCY RESPONSE AND TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT
TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT AND EMERGENCY RESPONSE INTERFACE
INTEGRATED RESPONSE FRAMEWORK
Effective emergency response relies on a cohesive framework that integrates traffic management
with emergency protocols. This integration ensures that traffic flow and emergency access
requirements are coordinated, minimising delays and optimising response actions for incidents
affecting personnel, vehicles, and equipment.



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 229
INCORPORATING TRAFFIC ELEMENTS INTO EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT PLANS
In addition to the requirements of the Emergency Preparedness and Response Plan Framework,
Contractors’ emergency response plans must include specific traffic-related components, such as
designated emergency access routes, vehicle incident response procedures, emergency contacts,
and communication protocols.
EMERGENCY ACCESS AND EGRESS
DESIGNATED EMERGENCY ROUTES

Emergency access routes must be designated across the site, encompassing main access roads,
tunnels, haul routes, and critical infrastructure. These routes must be clearly marked in both site-
wide and contractor-specific TMPs, site plans and diagrams to ensure consistent awareness and
implementation.
UNOBSTRUCTED ACCESS POINTS AND ROUTES
Emergency site access points and routes must remain unobstructed at all times to allow swift entry
and exit during incidents.
Regular inspections must be conducted to ensure these access points remain clear of equipment,
materials, and unauthorised vehicles. Any obstructions must be reported immediately to the Traffic
Department and the ER/PMC.
PARKING FOR EMERGENCY SERVICES
Contractors must allocate and sign designated parking bays for emergency service vehicles, marked
as “Emergency Services Parking Area.” These bays must remain accessible and free from any
unauthorised vehicles or materials.
EMERGENCY NOTIFICATION AND COMMUNICATION
RELIABLE COMMUNICATION DEVICES AND SITE-WIDE NOTIFICATION SYSTEM
        A comprehensive site-wide emergency notification system, such as radio communications,
loudspeakers, and visual alarms, should be established to alert all personnel, including vehicle and
mobile plant operators, in the event of an emergency. This system must ensure notifications are
clearly heard and understood by operators in all areas, including confined spaces such as tunnels.
COORDINATION WITH SITE AND EXTERNAL EMERGENCY SERVICES
External emergency services should be provided with comprehensive site access information,
including emergency vehicle routes, designated access points, and contact details for the project’s
emergency response team and incident management personnel.
Contractors should ensure emergency contacts are readily accessible to all drivers and operators,
including heavy plant operators, and that these contacts are also available to external delivery
drivers.
CCTV MONITORING AND INCIDENT DETECTION
Rogun JSC’s security personnel monitor site activities through CCTV, focusing on high-risk zones
such as tunnel entrances, main access roads, and areas prone to rockfall and landslide hazards.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 230
Security personnel should receive training in emergency response protocols to enhance incident
detection and response coordination.
The feasibility of extending CCTV coverage to tunnels should be reviewed and agreed upon by
Rogun JSC and the ER/PMC). If approved, CCTV systems should be strategically positioned to
enable real-time monitoring of high-risk zones and facilitate a prompt, coordinated response to
incidents.
When CCTV monitoring personnel observe traffic violations or identify other issues, they will need to
report them to the ER/PMC for follow up action.
INCIDENT RESPONSE AND REPORTING PROTOCOLS
      Emergency Scenarios Requiring Response: The following emergency scenarios require
       distinct response protocols to safeguard personnel and mitigate potential hazards. As such,
       they must be identified as potential emergencies in Contractor Emergency Preparedness and
       Response Plan, with appropriate measures to prepare and respond to incidents of these
       types. Road traffic accidents involving injury or fatality or interrupting work
      Fire or explosion involving a vehicle or load
      Vehicle entrapment or rollover in tunnels or confined spaces
      Driver or personnel injury/fatality due to accidents
      Vehicle breakdowns in high-risk or extreme weather conditions
      Property damage from vehicle incidents, including fire containment
      Total or partial load loss during transit
      Security threats involving vehicles or personnel
TRAINING, REPORTING AND DRILL REQUIREMENTS
As required by Contractor EPRPs, regular emergency drills should be conducted to evaluate the
effectiveness of traffic incident response procedures, emergency vehicle access, and
communication protocols. These drills should involve coordination between on-site and external
emergency services to verify alignment, readiness, and effective response coordination across all
involved entities.
Also as required by EPRPs, traffic incidents and mobile equipment emergency events should be
reported in accordance with the formal incident reporting procedure, followed by an investigation
and production of a corrective action plan.


DRIVER/OPERATOR COMPETENCY AND TRAFFIC SAFETY TRAINING
DRIVER AND OPERATOR COMPETENCY REQUIREMENTS
Only competent drivers may operate light vehicles, site vehicles, mobile machinery, and other
vehicles on-site. All operators must meet the licensing, qualification, and training requirements set
by their employers and Rogun JSC, and Tajikistan laws.
As noted previously, Contractors (as well as the Rogun JSC and the ER/PMC, must verify and
document driver competency before granting site authorisation. A site driving license must be issued
to each operator upon confirmation that all licensing, training, and competency checks have been



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 231
completed for the vehicle or mobile equipment they are authorized to operate. The following
requirements apply:
      Licensing and Certification: Operators must provide valid licenses and certifications as
       required by national regulations and site-specific requirements.
      Training Verification: Contractors must document that operators have completed traffic safety
       training, including project- and vehicle-specific driving rules and procedures.
      Annual Compliance Checks: Contractors must conduct annual reviews of licenses and
       driving records for all operators to maintain compliance with competency standards.
      Competency Assessments: Records of driver competency evaluations must be maintained
       from the recruitment process, with periodic assessments scheduled to ensure ongoing
       fitness and compliance.
Drivers must be physically fit to operate assigned vehicles and must meet the minimum health
requirements specified by national regulations.
On-road safety awareness.
CONTRACTOR TMP REQUIREMENTS
        Each Contractor's TMP must include a description of the systems they will implement to
train, monitor, and enforce driver competency and traffic safety compliance within their work areas.
This must include internal procedures for verifying training completion, conducting ongoing driver
assessments, managing non-compliance, and maintaining accessible training records.
TRAFFIC SAFETY TRAINING PROGRAMS
As noted, all drivers must complete both standard traffic safety training and job-specific or
contractor-specific training before operating any vehicle or equipment on-site. Training requirements
will Abe reviewed and approved as part of the Contractor’s TMP.
TRAINING COMPONENTS
General traffic safety training that will be nandatory for all drivers will include:
      Pedestrian Safety: Drivers must recognize that pedestrians have the right-of-way in all
       locations.
      Speed Limit Compliance: Site-specific speed limits, enforcement measures.
      Defensive Driving: Safe driving practices, hazard perception, and risk management in
       construction zones.
      Emergency Response Procedures: Understanding emergency routes, vehicle evacuation
       protocols, and communication during incidents.
      Fitness for Duty Requirements: Health and fatigue management standards for all drivers.
Job Specific and Contractor Specific Training
      Emergency Response Procedures: Understanding emergency routes, vehicle evacuation
       protocols, and communication during incidents
      Heavy Goods Vehicle (HGV) and Oversized Load Operators: Load stability, braking
       distances, and high-risk manoeuvring techniques.
      Mobile Equipment Operators: Safe operation of excavators, loaders, dump trucks, and
       cranes under site conditions.


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                             Page | 232
      Shuttle Bus and Personnel Transport Drivers: Passenger safety, drop-off and pick-up zone
       protocols, and incident management.
      Tunnel and Confined Space Driving: Visibility challenges, ventilation hazards, two-way traffic
       coordination, and communication requirements.
Contractor-Specific Training
      Each contractor must deliver additional training tailored to their specific work areas and
       vehicle types.
Contractors are responsible for maintaining ongoing traffic awareness among their workforce
through:
      Coverage of key site-wide and Contractor-specific rules in induction training.
      Regular toolbox talks and safety campaigns that reinforce critical traffic and road safety
       behaviours, covering safe crossing practices, congestion risks and overtaking restrictions,
       PPE requirements, and road condition awareness.
      Immediate communication and re-training in response to any changes in site conditions,
       control measures, or traffic routes. Changes to traffic routes, speed limits, or safety protocols
       must be communicated site-wide in a thorough, consistent, and timely manner to ensure
       effective change management without introducing new risks.
Training for drivers must also cover personal safety practices, highlighting specific instructions on
how to ensure individual safety and protect other road users. Training must include completion of
pre-start and pre-shift checks for all vehicles and equipment, ensuring driver competency in using
safety checklists to confirm equipment readiness prior to operation.
PROJECT INDUCTIONS
All personnel, including workers, contractors, and visitors, must complete a site-wide induction
approved by Rogun JSC and the ER/PMC before accessing the site. Contractors are responsible for
ensuring their workforce also completes contractor-specific inductions covering job-specific hazards
and requirements.
Inductions must include essential traffic and road safety protocols to ensure compliance with site
regulations and to promote a safe working environment.
The ER/PMC is responsible for preparing and implementing the on-site traffic safety and hazard
awareness training, which is provided as part of the induction for all direct employees and
subcontractors. This will be conducted with the assistance of the Rogun JSC security and traffic
department to ensure consistency and compliance with project standards.
At a minimum, the induction shall include critical traffic and road safety information, such as:
      Speed limits, right-of-way rules, and adherence to traffic signage.
      Mandatory use of seatbelts, prohibition of speeding, and a strict no-mobile-phone policy
       while driving.
      Overview of mandatory road rules for drivers, with an emphasis on driver fitness for work,
       competency standards, and pre-start checklist requirements.
Contractors are additionally required to conduct their own worker-specific inductions that cover the
unique risks and conditions associated with their designated work areas, including specific traffic
routes, vehicles, and mobile plant within their scope of operations.



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 233
Visitor inductions may omit operational details specific to workers but must include all relevant traffic
and safety information applicable to their on-site presence to maintain their safety and the safety of
others.
DEFENSIVE DRIVING AND INCIDENT PREVENTION
Defensive driving techniques are mandatory for all drivers to reduce collision risks, with additional
emphasis for those operating heavy machinery or navigating high-risk areas. Defensive driving
training must address:
      Safe speed and braking techniques, particularly on steep grades or loose surfaces.
      Procedures for low-visibility conditions such as fog, dust, and nighttime driving.
      Anticipatory driving to manage potential hazards, including the possibility of rockfall,
       landslides, or sudden wildlife appearances.
Contractors must verify that all drivers understand and demonstrate competency in these
techniques, supported by practical evaluations conducted under actual or simulated site conditions.
ASSESSMENT, MONITORING, AND COMPLIANCE
Ongoing assessment and monitoring are critical to ensuring driver competency and adherence to
traffic safety standards. Contractors must establish systems that routinely verify compliance with
training protocols, licensing, and health standards.
Rogun JSC, or appointed representatives, shall:
      Conduct periodic audits and inspections to verify that driver competencies align with TMP
       and legal requirements.
      Mandate retraining or corrective actions for any instances of non-compliance, unsafe driving
       practices, or gaps in competency.
      Document audit findings, with immediate actions required to rectify any identified training or
       competency deficiencies.
Training records and competency assessments should be accessible to Rogun JSC and the
ER/PMC for auditing purposes, with immediate corrective measures enacted if gaps in competency
or safety compliance are identified.
Contractors should actively monitor and enforce compliance within their Lots and operational areas,
with supervisors responsible for overseeing driver behaviour, speed adherence, and general traffic
flow.


ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES
PROJECT ORGANISATIONAL STRUCTURE
Rogun JSC holds overall responsibility for construction and operational activities at Rogun HPP,
including traffic safety and contractor management. Traffic management is currently overseen by
Rogun JSC’s Security Department. The Employer’s Representative (ER--and in the future a Project
Management Consultant (PMC)) manages contractor traffic operations for both construction and
operational activities in coordination with Rogun JSC.

ROGUN JSC SECURITY DEPARTMENT: ROLES IN TRAFFIC AND SAFETY OVERSIGHT
The department is responsible for ensuring compliance with TMP requirements, investigating traffic-
related incidents, and coordinating with the Employer’s Representative/PMC to maintain consistent
enforcement across all project areas.
Key roles within the Security Department include:
       Head of the Traffic Safety Section - Oversees overall compliance, risk assessment, and
        enforcement of TMP measures.
       Traffic Safety Specialist - Conducts site inspections, monitors compliance, documents
        violations, and recommends corrective actions.
The full scope of responsibilities for the Security Department in traffic management is outlined in
Rogun HPP JSC, 2021 Job Description Documents.
SITE-WIDE COMPLIANCE AND TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT ACCOUNTABILITY
PROJECT MANAGEMENT ACCOUNTABILITY
This framework TMP establishes requirements for the maintenance and operation of all mobile
vehicles and equipment on the Rogun HPP site. It applies to Rogun JSC, Contractors, and all
personnel operating within the site, including third-party service providers and visitors. It also
establishes the minimum standards for Contractors to develop Lot-specific TMPs for their
operations.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                            October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                      Page | 237
Rogun JSC is responsible for implementing, monitoring, and enforcing this TMP across all Lots and
site operations. On behalf of Rogun JSC, the Employer’s Representative (current) and PMC (future)
will oversee compliance, conduct audits, and ensure that all Contractors align with the TMP's
requirements.
MANDATORY COMPLIANCE AND MINIMUM STANDARDS

All site users, including Rogun JSC personnel, Contractors, subcontractors, and third-party site
visitors, must comply with the requirements of this framework TMP.
Contractors must align their Lot-specific TMPs with the site-wide TMP and implement traffic control
measures that meet or exceed the standards outlined in this document.
In this framework TMP:
      "Must" statements define mandatory and enforceable requirements aligned with Project
       safety standards, Tajikistan laws, and international best practices.
      "Should" statements indicate recommended industry best practices that enhance traffic
       safety but are not compulsory unless specified in contractual requirements.


STAKEHOLDER ENGAGEMENT AND COORDINATION
SITE-WIDE ENGAGEMENT AND PARTICIPATION
CONTRACTOR COORDINATION
Stakeholders engagement is an integral part of the preparation of this framework TMP. To this end,
Contractors (key stakeholder) must actively participate in TMP implementation within the areas they
cover and ensure their drivers and vehicles comply with their TMP and the site-wide TMP in other
areas. The ER/PMC will facilitate mandatory coordination meetings with contractors to review TMP
updates, assess compliance, and enforce corrective actions where necessary.
Key coordination requirements include:
      Regular Contractor Meetings: Contractors must attend monthly TMP coordination meetings
       led by the ER/PMC. These meetings will cover TMP updates, traffic flow adjustments,
       incident findings, and required corrective measures.
      Contractor Feedback Mechanisms: Contractors must establish internal processes to report
       traffic-related concerns, suggest improvements, and identify on-site hazards. These reports
       must be submitted to the ER/PMC for review and, where applicable, integration into TMP
       revisions.
      Communication Protocols: Contractors must comply with defined reporting lines for traffic
       incidents and near-misses, ensuring prompt reporting to ER/PMC. Timely communication is
       required to support coordinated responses and enforcement of traffic safety measures.
STAKEHOLDER COMMUNICATION AND FEEDBACK INTEGRATION
The ER/PMC will establish feedback mechanisms to gather insights from contractors, community
members, and government authorities. These inputs will guide TMP updates, ensuring practices
remain responsive to stakeholder needs.
Formal communication procedures will ensure significant TMP adjustments are effectively
communicated to all stakeholders:

Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                             Page | 238
      Document and report stakeholder feedback, communications, and corrective actions as part
       of routine TMP monitoring.
      Notify contractors and community stakeholders of significant TMP updates or new protocols
       through structured communications to ensure alignment with revised standards


MONITORING, REPORTING AND REVIEW
MONITORING AND INSPECTION REQUIREMENTS
Regular monitoring and inspection activities are essential to ensuring driver and pedestrian
adherence to TMP standards, assessing the effectiveness of implemented controls, and addressing
high-priority risks identified in the ESIA traffic assessment and other relevant project documents.
Top management should visibly demonstrate commitment to traffic incident prevention by
participating in traffic safety audits, conducting regular inspections, and attending OHS meetings
focused on traffic management. They must also comply with relevant requirements, including use of
safety belts, pre-start checklists, and proper PPE, as well as observing pedestrian rules.
Monitoring activities should be tailored to address high-priority risks and controls on-site, as outlined
in Section 3 and Section 17, which details the risk management strategy and phased approach to
TMP implementation.
Key monitoring activities should include the following:
      Daily Inspections: As required by the OHS Management Plan and Contractor OHS Plans,
       vehicle operators should conduct pre-start inspections using a standardised checklist to
       verify equipment readiness and identify immediate hazards. Contractor supervisors are
       responsible for ensuring these inspections are completed daily.
      Weekly Contractor Site Inspections: Routine HSE site inspections performed by contractor
       supervisors to monitor compliance with TMP requirements, using a structured audit checklist
       for traffic management. Weekly inspections should verify adherence to speed limits, road
       conditions, and vehicle safety.
      Random Speed Monitoring: Weekly random speed surveys, conducted with handheld speed
       guns in various locations, prioritising tunnels, areas near villages and schools to ensure
       compliance with established speed limits.
      Casual Observations. Senior managers, HSE managers and specialists, and supervisors
       should alert to traffic conditions and identify unsafe vehicle condition or operation.
      Traffic Flow Monitoring: Assess traffic flow at congestion hotspots and before any planned
       route changes to evaluate viability, identify potential risks, and adjust control measures as
       necessary.
      Alcohol and Drug Testing: Where deemed appropriate and in accordance with Tajikistan
       laws, random testing for alcohol and drugs may be conducted for vehicle operators and
       heavy equipment personnel, with results documented and reported in alignment with relevant
       E&S reporting requirements.
With the exception of minor issues that are not repeated, all instances of noncompliant vehicle
operation or condition must be documented and reported to the HSE manager of the relevant
Contractor and to the ER/PMC.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                      October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                Page | 239
All formal inspections and audits should be documented, with findings and corrective actions made
available to the HSE manager of the relevant Contractor, and summarized in monthly progress
reports to the ER/PMC. Documentation should identify all deficiencies identified during inspections,
actions taken at the time, corrective actions that must still be implemented, and reporting
requirements (e.g. reports that corrective actions are completed). .
REPORTING PROCEDURES FOR TRAFFIC NON-CONFORMANCES AND INCIDENTS
Contractors must implement formal procedures for reporting traffic-related non-conformances, near
misses, hazards, and incidents. Reporting should be structured to allow workers to report traffic
hazards or unsafe behaviours to supervisors, who will then escalate reports through the contractor’s
HSE management chain to Rogun JSC.
Contractor management are responsible for ensuring corrective actions are implemented in
response to traffic non-conformances, with accountability measures in place to prevent recurrence.
Formal written procedures should be established at both contractor and site-wide levels to address:
      Non-Conformances: Processes for investigating and resolving incidents of non-compliance,
       with a clear escalation path for recurring issues.
      Investigation and Disciplinary Actions: Formal investigation processes for significant non-
       conformances, with disciplinary action as necessary to reinforce adherence to traffic
       management standards.
Traffic-related reports, including incidents, hazards, and corrective actions, should be compiled into
a formal report and submitted to PMC/ER on a scheduled basis, such as monthly. These reports
provide oversight of on-site traffic safety and are integral to ensuring ongoing compliance.
KEY PERFORMANCE INDICATORS AND MONITORING METRICS
Contractors should monitor key performance indicators (KPIs) to measure TMP effectiveness and
compliance. Suggested KPIs include:
      Number of Traffic Incidents: Total incidents reported, categorised by severity, to track trends
       and identify high-risk areas.
      Compliance with Training Requirements: Percentage of drivers and operators completing
       mandatory training programs.
      Non-Conformance Resolution: Timeframes for resolving traffic-related non-conformances,
       from initial report to corrective action completion.
      Vehicle Inspections and Maintenance: Frequency of vehicle safety inspections, repair trends,
       and roadworthiness status.
      Road and Site Conditions: Records of road blockages, surface condition assessments, and
       any required road maintenance actions.
KPIs should be reported in monthly progress reports and reviewed regularly to inform ongoing TMP
improvements and adjustments as needed.
RECORD MANAGEMENT
       Effective record management is critical to ensuring compliance with safety standards,
supporting ongoing risk assessment, and maintaining accountability for traffic and safety
management at the Rogun HPP site. The Labor Code of Tajikistan emphasises workplace




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                    October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                              Page | 240
certification, which necessitates detailed record-keeping to demonstrate compliance with safety
regulations and to facilitate the monitoring of site conditions.
RECORD TYPES

Contractor TMPs must require well maintained documentation of traffic and safety-related activities
to ensure effective management and compliance. Example records to maintain include:
      Driver and Operator Records: Validity of driver licenses, including expiry dates and renewals.
      Site Risk Assessments: Documentation of traffic and transport-related risk assessments.
      Audit and Inspection Reports: Internal and external audit reports, including inspection
       findings.
      Incident and Non-Conformance Records: Records of traffic-related incidents, near-misses,
       and non-conformances, including corrective actions taken.
      Road Design and Engineering Approvals: Certificates, engineering sign-offs, and structural
       assessments related to road design.
      Training and Induction Records: Documentation of traffic safety training programs, including
       attendance logs and evaluation result.
RECORD RETENTION AND CONFIDENTIALITY
Records must be managed and retained through a secure and organised system in compliance with
Tajikistan legislation and relevant contractual obligations. The system must ensure accessibility to
authorised personnel and adherence to specified retention timelines
TMP FRAMEWORK REVIEW AND UPDATE REQUIREMENTS
KEY TRIGGERS FOR UPDATES
       The TMP should be reviewed and updated in response to:
      Traffic Route Changes: Adjustments to haul roads, tunnel access points, or other key routes.
      New Equipment: Introduction of machinery that alters traffic patterns or creates new risks.
      Operational Shifts: Changes in construction phases or traffic volumes requiring updated
       controls.
      Incidents or Near Misses: Traffic-related events necessitating reassessment of measures.
      Regulatory Changes: Updates to laws or standards affecting TMP requirements.
      Stakeholder Feedback: Input from contractors, local communities and traffic safety
       personnel, highlighting gaps or opportunities for improvement.
      Environmental Changes: Adverse weather, landslides, or structural modifications affecting
       accessibility.
CHANGE MANAGEMENT AND DOCUMENTATION

All TMP revisions must:
      Be recorded in a controlled register for traceability and compliance.
      Undergo review and approval by the ER/PMC prior to implementation.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                             Page | 241
COMMUNICATION OF UPDATES
Revised TMP measures must be clearly communicated to all personnel through:
      Updated inductions and training sessions.
      Toolbox talks addressing specific changes.
      Posted notices at key access points and operational areas.
TRANSITION TO OPERATIONS
The TMP must address significant traffic changes during the transition to operational phases,
including:
      Replacing temporary controls with permanent systems.
      Developing operational traffic management protocols.
      Integrating permanent access routes, land-use zones, and operational areas.
PHASED IMPLEMENTATION STRATEGY
RISK-BASED APPROACH

TMP measures must be implemented using a structured, risk-informed approach that prioritises:
      High-Risk Hazards: Controls targeting severe risks, such as vehicle-pedestrian collisions,
       which pose significant safety threats.
      Hazard Prevalence: Addressing both isolated risks (e.g., hazards specific to tunnels or
       intersections) and systemic hazards (e.g., site-wide traffic issues).
      Practicality: Ensuring measures are feasible and aligned with operational constraints,
       timelines, and available resources.
      Project Milestones: Adapting controls to reflect construction phases and evolving traffic
       patterns as the project progresses.
PHASED ROLLOUT
he phased rollout ensures TMP measures are introduced systematically to address hazards as they
emerge. Immediate actions focus on mitigating urgent risks, while intermediate and long-term
measures refine controls and establish permanent traffic management systems.
A detailed example of this phased approach is provided in the Phased Implementation Roadmap
which outlines proposed actions, timelines, and responsibilities for TMP deployment.
IMPLEMENTATION PRINCIPLES
How and when control measures are introduced on-site shall be guided by the following principles:
      Prioritisation of High-Risk Hazards: Ensuring that critical risks are addressed first to
       safeguard workers and operations.
      Timeframes Linked to Risk Severity: Tackling urgent hazards early while phasing in
       measures for lower-risk scenarios over time.
      Adaptability: Allowing for adjustments based on changing site conditions, stakeholder
       feedback, and evolving construction requirements.
As outlined in Section 3, the phased approach must be supported by a robust, collaborative risk
assessment process. This process should be led by Rogun JSC in consultation with the ER/PMC

and contractor managers. This ensures the roadmap remains dynamic, focused, and aligned with
project-specific risks, objectives, and operational realities.

CONCLUSION
The purpose of the Traffic Management Plan (TMP) Framework is to set out principles, processes,
timelines, measures and steps to safely manage vehicular and pedestrian traffic during
construction. This TMP applies to all Project employees and subcontractors moving material,
machinery and human resources to and from construction zones.
The objectives of the TMP are to:
      Avoid or minimise potential impacts of construction activities on road safety
      Avoid or minimise potential impacts on the community and other road uses with respect to
       traffic and transport.
      Identify actions to minimise and mitigate impacts on road safety, traffic flow and access.
This TMP will assist in meeting the Project’s obligations under the national legislation of Tajikistan
and in ensuring alignment with the World Bank Group’s Environmental, Health, and Safety (EHS)
Guidelines.
The movement of vehicles associated with the construction of the Project poses a risk to workers,
the community and environment. The potential impacts and risks associated with construction traffic
include:
      Potential incidents, injuries or fatalities associated with vehicles, roadway hazards or
       obstructions.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                      October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                                Page | 247
      Conflicts between road users due to increased usage of public roads by light and heavy
       vehicles.
      Property damage to roadside properties, water sources etc. from road construction-activities
      Environmental impacts from road construction and use, including impacts to air quality,
       noise, biodiversity values, water quality.


For these purposes, each Contractor employed at Rogun Hydropower Project (the Project) will
prepare and implement a Traffic Management Plan or Contractor’s Traffic Management Plan (TMP
or C-TMP) that is consistent with this Framework. The Plan will be reviewed and approved by the
Contractor’s Project Manager and submitted to the Employer’s Representative (ER) and/or the
Project Management Consultant (ER/PMC) for review. Once approved, it shall be diligently
implemented by the Contractor.
New Contractors must have an approved Plan before mobilizing workers. Existing Contractors must
have an approved Plan within six months of the date that World Bank financing is provided to the
Project or as otherwise required by the contract. If an existing Contractor has a TMP that has been
approved by the ER, a new plan is not needed if the ER verifies the existing plan is equivalent to
what is required by this Framework, or if the Contractor makes sufficient changes to the existing
plan that the ER determines it is equivalent.
The purpose of this Framework is to identify the minimum requirements for the Contractors’ TMPs,
and to ensure the Plans contain the required content, although the Plan may vary based on the
potential traffic hazards and risks of the works the Contractor is required to perform.
Note that the TMP Framework is to be implemented in conjunction with the Construction ESMP, the
Biodiversity Management Plan, the Grievance Redress Mechanism, the Security Management Plan,
the Worker’s Health and Safety Plan, the Workers Code of Conduct, the Waste Management Plan,
the Spill Prevention and Emergency Response Plan, the Air Quality Management and Dust Control
Plan, the Quarry Management Plan, the Drainage, Erosion and Sediment Control Plan, the Noise
and Vibration Management Plan, the Water Quality Monitoring Plan, the Construction Works
Monitoring Plan, and the Air Quality.

38. OFF-SITE TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT PLAN
 INTRODUCTION
 Background
 This Offsite Traffic Management Plan (TMP) Framework sets out a set of generic requirements for
 traffic management during the construction and operation phases of the Project. It provides general
 guidelines, principles steps and Good International Industry Practices (GIIP) that can be adapted to
 the project-specific traffic management plan as part of the overarching Environmental and Social
 Management Plan (ESMP) and other relevant environmental and social risk due diligence
 documents of the project. Accordingly, the objectives of this framework TMP include but not limited
 to establish general requirements of traffic management to be implemented by the project proponent
 and contractor to avoid and minimize traffic disturbance and ensure the safety of public and project
 workers during the project construction and operation.
 This TMP Framework is intended to be used for traffic management during the construction and
 operation stage of a project which may have potential impacts on road traffic and related
 public/worker safety concerns caused by road traffic. These include e.g. direct road construction or
 maintenance, construction activities occupying road or sidewalk, construction vehicles/equipment
 entering public roads, and construction vehicles/equipment through local community roads, etc.
 During the preparation, construction and operations, a project onsite -specific traffic management
 plan using this TMP as a general framework, taking into account project-specific situation and
 demand, will be developed as part of the project’s Contractors ESMP or other E & S documents as
 appropriate. In addition, during the implementation of the project, this TMP (or the project contractor
 specific TMP) will be incorporated into the bidding documents and latterly the construction contracts,
 as part of the environmental and social management specifications.
 Purpose and Applicability Traffic Management Plan Framework
 Each Contractor employed at Rogun Hydropower Project (the Project) will prepare and implement a
 Traffic Management Plan or Contractor’s Traffic Management Plan (TMP or C-TMP) that is
 consistent with this Framework. The Plan will be reviewed and approved by the Contractor’s Project
 Manager and submitted to the Employer’s Representative (ER) and/or the Project Management
 Consultant (ER/PMC) for review. Once approved, it shall be diligently implemented by the
 Contractor.
 New Contractors must have an approved Plan before mobilizing workers. Existing Contractors must
 have an approved Plan within six months of the date that World Bank financing is provided to the
 Project or as otherwise required by the contract. If an existing Contractor has a TMP that has been
 approved by the ER, a new plan is not needed if the ER verifies the existing plan is equivalent to
 what is required by this Framework, or if the Contractor makes sufficient changes to the existing
 plan that the ER determines it is equivalent.
 The purpose of this Framework is to identify the minimum requirements for the Contractors’ TMPs,
 and to ensure the Plans contains the required content, although the Plan may vary based on the
 potential traffic hazards and risks of the works the Contractor is required to perform.

Scope
This Construction Site Framework Traffic Management Plan is a reference guide for contractors to
prepare, implement and manage traffic at their construction sites through sharing some good
practices. This framework TMP is not intended to be a duplication of the Traffic and Transport
assessment nor a substitute to Contractors TMP. However, this framework TMP does not apply to
areas outside the construction workplace where the contractor has no management control and for
which a separate TMP has been prepared for Offsite Traffic. This Framework TMP should be read in
conjunction with the following documents/reports:
       On-Site Traffic Management Plan (Volume 3, A9a)
       Security Management Plan (Volume 3, A7)
       Occupational Health and Safety Management Plans prepared by Contractors to meet
        requirements of Rogun JSC’s OHS Management Plan Framework
       Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP) (Volume 3, A1)
OVERVIEW
This Off-Site Traffic Management Plan (hereafter referred to as ‘OS-TMP’) has been prepared for
the Rogun Open Joint Stock Company (JSC) (hereafter referred to as ‘Rogun JSC’) by WSP UK
Limited (hereafter referred to as ‘WSP’) for the Rogun Hydropower Project (HPP) (hereafter referred
to as ‘the Project’).
The Government of Tajikistan established Rogun JSC to own and operate the Project. The Project
Management Group (PMG) for Energy Facilities Construction, under the President of the Republic of
Tajikistan, is the implementing entity responsible for managing the construction of the Project.
Rogun JSC oversees both the construction and long-term operation of the Project, which is currently
undergoing an extensive phase of construction and partial operation, with two turbines already in
active use.
The Project is supported by a lender consortium, led by the World Bank and collectively referred to
as the ‘Lenders,’ which is considering financing the Project. Compliance with the environmental and
social policies of the Lenders, aligned under the overarching Environmental and Social Framework
(ESF), is essential to meet funding requirements. These requirements are based on the World Bank
ESF, including adherence to the World Bank General Environmental, Health, and Safety (EHS)
Guidelines: Community Health and Safety and consistent with Tajikistan extant E & S framework.
TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT AND ESIA ALIGNMENT
This document has been developed in alignment with Traffic and Transport Section of this
Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for construction and operation of the Rogun
HPP, and in conjunction with the On-Site Traffic Management Plan (Volume 3, A9a). It forms a key
component of the traffic management strategy framework required by Volume 3, A1: Environmental
and Social Management Plan (ESMP) of this ESIA.
The OS-TMP integrates findings from evaluations of current off-site traffic practices conducted in
consultation with Rogun JSC, Contractors, and the Employer’s Representative. It addresses
identified risks related to transport activities beyond the Project boundaries resulting from Project
traffic and ensures alignment with the ESMP requirements, Project objectives, and World Bank ESF
standards.



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                             Page | 250
Traffic and Transport
Traffic accidents have been decreasing in Tajikistan in recent years, from 1303 recorded incidents in
2017 to 1096 incidents in 2022. Deaths due to traffic incidents also decreased nationally from 2017-
2021, from 431 to 375 deaths, although an increase in mortality was recorded in 2022 (416 deaths).
Locally, in the Rasht zone, both accident rates and fatality rates have remained relatively steady
over the same period. The fewest accidents occurred in 2021 (3) and the fewest fatalities in 2019
(2). The most accidents occurred in 2022 (11) and the most deaths in 2020 (7). Although evidence
lacks on the traffic accidents for the Project area specifically, both women and men FGDs highlight
road safety concerns of communities and the poor road conditions due to ongoing construction and
use of heavy trucks.
This section presents the baseline data for the Traffic and Transport Assessment for the Project.
The information presented here is to be read in conjunction with Traffic and Transport Section of this
ESIA. No primary transport baseline data collection was undertaken for the 2014 ESIA. The baseline
conditions at the site reflect existing operations plus the construction work that is ongoing.
Secondary baseline data sources have been utilized through desk-based studies to identify key
issues based on existing maps, previous studies, satellite imagery and other relevant material.
Tajikistan Transport Network
Tajikistan is a landlocked and mountainous country, surrounded by Afghanistan, the People’s
Republic of China (PRC), Kyrgyzstan, and Uzbekistan. Approximately 93% of Tajikistan’s terrain is
mountainous, complicating transport and transit. Most of the transport infrastructure was built during
the Soviet period and was designed to optimize the Soviet system of inter-republic linkages between
other Soviet republics. After Tajikistan became independent in 1991, relationships between
Tajikistan and the neighboring countries changed and the Tajik Civil War began, affecting the
transport networks and reducing inter-country traffic volumes and trade.
As a result, passenger transport reduced by three quarters, freight transport by two thirds, and
freight turnover by three quarters during 1990–1996. As such, government funding for the transport
sector was significantly reduced which has since resulted in the deterioration of the nation’s
transport infrastructure due to lack of maintenance (ADB, 2021).
National Road Network
The dominant form of transport infrastructure in Tajikistan is roads, which play a key role in
facilitating domestic and international connectivity. Road connectivity is oriented mainly toward
Uzbekistan, accounting for more than half of the main road border crossing points (BCPs), as well
as towards Kyrgyzstan through several BCPs. The nearest seaport to Tajikistan is Bandar Abbas,
Iran (approximately 2,500km from Dushanbe, a 35-hour drive) which can be accessed through
Afghanistan, but the available transport modes to reach the port are limited, and recent political
stability and violence in Afghanistan makes transit through the country difficult.
The ADB 2021 transport sector assessment indicates that around 56% of Tajikistan’s roads are in
poor condition, particularly smaller local roads (ADB, 2021).
Public Transport
Public transport exists in cities in Tajikistan. In Dushanbe, buses and white vans (marshrutkas) with
line numbers run to most destinations within Dushanbe. A refurbished Grand Bus Station opened in


Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                   October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                             Page | 251
Dushanbe in 2013 which serves passengers who are travelling to suburban areas, other Tajik cities
such as Bokhtar, Khujand and Khorog, and international destinations such as Termez (Uzbekistan),
Osh (Kyrgyzstan) and Moscow (Russia).
However, aside from this, rural Tajikistan does not benefit from an extensive public transportation
network. No buses or trains connect rural suburbs with urban centers. The main form of transport is
by car. Rural residents travel either in their own private vehicles or participate in a taxi-sharing
system with their neighbors in order to travel to local and regional centers. Some marshrutkas are
also available.
Roads in Proximity to the Project
Pamir Highway – (M41 / E60 / AH65)
The M41, more commonly referred to as the Pamir Highway, is an international road traversing the
Pamir Mountains through Afghanistan, Uzbekistan, Tajikistan, and Kyrgyzstan. In Tajikistan, the
Pamir Highway is divided into sections IB02, RB04, RB07. The RB07 section of the Pamir Highway
(M41) runs from border of Kyrgyzstan – Jirgital – Obigarm – Vahdat adjoining with RB04 to
Dushanbe, passing the Rogun HPP project site at Obigarm.
WSP visited this section of the M41 highway in September 2024 to assess its condition. The road is
a single carriageway highway with a single lane in either direction with bridges and tunnels to
traverse the mountainous terrain in which it sits. The asphalt used was of good quality, is wide and
clear, and had no obvious defects such as potholes in the approximately 50km stretch assessed by
WSP. Construction of the road was almost complete at the time of the visit and the program was
due to finish at the end of 2024. Final works being completed included adding bridge expansion
joints to the bridges crossing ravines along its length, adding in road markings, and fixing safety
barriers. WSP met with the Deputy Director of the Project Management Group for M41 (Obigarm-
Nurobod) who stated that the road will undergo a period of stress testing to ensure any defects are
identified and rectified before it is opened to the public in early 2025, as is currently planned.
M41 Obigarm-Nurobod Road Realignment Project
The Obigarm-Nurobod road section of the existing Pamir Highway (M41) will be inundated once the
HPP reservoir has filled to operating levels. The Obigarm-Nurobod Road Realignment Project will
provide a 75 km bypass road. The overall project was divided into 3 sections:
     The Obigarm–Tagi kamar section is about 30km long financed by ADB and OFID;
     The Tagi kamar–Nurobod section is about 44km long financed by the EBRD; and
     The 920-meter-long bridge and its approaches will be financed by AIIB.
These are referred to under “Section 1” and “Section 2” in Paragraph 14.3.8.
In 2019, an Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) was prepared for the Obigarm-
Nurobod Road Realignment Project by the Ministry of Transport of the Republic of Tajikistan. The
Project includes 13 new bridge constructions, rehabilitation of three existing bridges, three new
tunnel constructions and six village access roads.
Source: Central Asia Regional Economic Cooperation Corridors 2, 3 and 5 (Obigarm-Nurobod)

be completed by November 2025 as the existing highway section will be inundated by the reservoir
(Tajik Ministry of Transport, 2019).
Two major new roads are planned for the area surrounding the reservoir:
     One 55km road along the left bank of the lower part of the reservoir, from the dam to the main
      bridge which will cross the reservoir;
     One on the right bank, upper part of the reservoir, between the bridge and the town of Gharm,
      located approximately 50 km to the north-east.

     Section 1: Main road (M41) on the right bank in the lower part of the reservoir: a considerable

      shortly after the independence of Tajikistan (September 1991) and the constructed sections
      have deteriorated over the last 20 years. Recently, the Research and Design Institute in
      Dushanbe, the state agency responsible for planning and construction of roads, planned to
      finalize construction of the 76 km new road alignment, which also includes rehabilitation of the
      damaged sections.
     Section 2: Main bridge over the reservoir: the relocation of the international road also includes
      a major bridge with a span of 786 m.

Sections 4 and 5 are at the pre-feasibility stage of planning and will only be built as a result of the
Project. They are included within the Project’s assessment.
The KamarOb Valley road
The Kamarob Valley (also known as Kamarov) is a tributary valley on the right bank of the reservoir,
located partly within the flooding zone in Rasht District. Currently there are 21 settlements within the
valley and its tributary valleys, 9 of which are scheduled for resettlement and 12 of which will remain.
The whole valley is covered by the Boqi Rahimzoda jamoat, so named for the Tajik-Soviet writer
who was born in the valley. There is one road that goes into and out of the valley. The road
continues beyond the uppermost village, but is impassable by vehicle, and the next settlement
(Gorif) is a 48-hour walk away.21 This road passes through the mouth of the valley and will be
flooded. It is currently unknown if, how and when the right bank road will be connected to the
villages remaining within the valley. The total population of the valley (including Gorif) is
approximately 12,000, including approximately 2,000 in the non-resettled villages.
On-site discussions with residents in the upper valley confirmed heavy reliance on travel to
settlements outside of the valley to meet basic necessities, particularly Gharm and Rasht City. All
interviewed residents in September 2024 reported travelling to these settlements at least monthly,
usually utilizing taxi-sharing arrangements with their neighbors.
Accidents and Safety
According to 2016 WHO statistics, the country had an estimated road accident fatality rate per
100,000 population of 13.9 in 2021. For context, this figure is 6.7 and 15 per 100,000 for Europe and
the world respectively (WHO, 2024). Of the fatalities, the majority relate to 4-wheeler vehicles (69%),
19% relating to pedestrians, 9% 2 to 3-wheeler vehicles, cyclists 1% and others 2%. The country
does not comply with many UN Vehicle Safety Regulations, with the only compliance being import
inspections.
Accidents are often attributed to non-compliance with traffic rules by drivers and pedestrians, illegal
purchasing of drivers’ licenses and inadequate road infrastructure in the country. The country has
the highest road traffic accident rate in Central Asia with the WHO requesting advancing of efforts to
reduce rates.
The Project prepares quarterly OHS reports on overall OHS performance for submission to
authorities. The reports detail excess fatalities and serious incidents, particularly in relation to traffic
accidents. The contents of these documents are not universally known so the material of which are
unable to be reported in this baseline annex.

       There are a range of shift patterns for employees, including day and night 15-day shifts and

SITE ENTRANCE GATE
Access to the site in Rogun City is via a single access point, which is security and military controlled,
and is situated south of the main urban area of Rogun City and provides access to the construction
site and dam wall area.
As of December 2024, approximately 5,000 workers live off-site, with approximately 12,500 workers
living on the construction site. Off-site workers generally travel to the site on foot, car, taxi or bus.
Some contractors provide bus transport to and from off-site accommodation at the start/end of shift
times.
Shift Rotations
Most of the workforce (excluding office workers) are on a rotational shift pattern, working 15 days on
and off, on a 12-hour day or night shift. The majority of the workforce, especially if accommodated
on-site, return home for their rest period. Table 14-3 presents traffic flows on 15th September 2024

          WeBuild developed a TMP for the HPP Rogun Lot 2, dated 24 May 2023. The TMP was prepared to

          core activities. This plan serves to ensure that adequate procedures are in place to minimize effects
          due to the presence of the Project’s site vehicles on the local traffic on affected road sections. This
          plan is being implemented by the Employer for the entire Project site, Rogun JSC. Its
          implementation is supervised by the HSE team of the Employer’s Representative. However, given
          the practical issues of limited control over the entire site, the compliance is variable between the
          contractors, with Lot 2 contractors demonstrating the highest adherence to the requirements.

                 Bulldozers;

                 Cement mixer trucks;
                 Drilling machines;
                 Fuel trucks;
                 Water trucks; and
                 Pick-ups.

          out of the Project site frequently. The remaining site vehicles enter and exit the main core site daily.

          rapidly once the concreting works gain momentum.

TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT PLAN OVERVIEW AND FRAMEWORK
The traffic management strategy framework for the Project comprises two interconnected plans to
manage traffic-related risks comprehensively.
Volume 3, A9a: On-Site Traffic Management Plan (TMP) addresses traffic management within
Project boundaries, providing structured requirements and guidance to ensure safe, efficient, and
compliant operations on-site.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 259
REPORT PURPOSE
The OS-TMP Framework provides requirements and guidance for off-site traffic management,
focusing on activities beyond the Project boundaries, such as the use of public roads for delivery of
materials and goods, transport of oversized and complex loads, worker transportation, and other
logistics. Together, these plans establish a cohesive framework to manage traffic risks, optimise
transport operations, and safeguard workers, contractors, and the surrounding communities.
The development of this OS-TMP has been informed by findings from Traffic and Transport Section
of this ESIA, which assessed potential traffic impacts on communities, road users, pedestrian safety,
and the transport of hazardous and oversized loads. This document is aligned with the findings and
the mitigation and enhancement measures identified in the assessment, ensuring that off-site traffic
risks are managed in accordance with Project objectives and Lender’s ESF requirements.
This document is designed to adapt to the evolving nature of the Project and will remain a living
document to reflect changing conditions, transport demands, and stakeholder feedback.
OBJECTIVES
The primary objectives of this OS-TMP Framework are to:
       Establish a structured and standardised framework for managing off-site transport activities,
        including the movement of materials, equipment, and workers along public routes, including
        from Dushanbe to the Project, and thus ensure safe, efficient, and compliant operations.
       Minimise off-site traffic risks to public road users, local communities, and Project personnel
        by addressing logistical challenges, implementing targeted risk mitigation measures, and
        safeguarding community safety through planned and communicated transport routes.
       Ensure all off-site transport activities comply with Tajikistan’s legal and regulatory
        requirements, including those of the Ministry of Transport, as well as international standards
        outlined below.
       Facilitate the safe and efficient movement of oversized and complex loads, ensuring
        adherence to route-specific requirements, road safety protocols, and hazard control
        measures.
       Support Rogun JSC and the Project Management Consultant (PMC) in supervising
        Contractor compliance with traffic and transport requirements. Note: As of early 2025, an
        Employer’s Representative (ER) acted on behalf of Rogun JSC to supervise environmental
        and social performance of Contractors. When international financing becomes available, the
        ER will be replaced by a Project Management Consultant. Reference to the ER or the PMC
        should be taken as a reference to either or both.

APPLICABLE LAWS, STANDARDS AND GUIDELINES
This document has been informed and developed in alignment with key national legislation,
international standards, and regulatory frameworks governing off-site traffic and transport operations
in Tajikistan.
Tajikistan National Laws And Standards
Government Resolution 779/2006 – Oversized Load Transport

Governs the transport of oversized loads in Tajikistan, requiring Ministry of Transport oversight and
coordination with the State Traffic Police to ensure safe passage and assess infrastructure suitability
along designated routes.
Code Of Road Transport Of The Republic Of Tajikistan (Law No. 1689)

Establishes the legal framework for vehicle operations on public roads, including specific standards
for oversized and hazardous load transport. This law governs driver licensing, vehicle compliance,
speed limits, and access controls to ensure safe and reliable transport activities.
Law Of The Republic Of Tajikistan "On Roads And Road Activities" (Article 46)
Regulates the safe movement of dangerous goods by road, prescribing protocols for the secure and
compliant.
Rules For Passing By Highways Of Vehicles With Loads Exceeding Established Norms (2006):
Issued by the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan, this decree provides detailed procedures
and requirements for the transport of vehicles carrying loads that surpass standard weight and
dimension limits on highways. It mandates special authorisation, route suitability assessments, and
coordination with local traffic authorities to ensure the safe and compliant movement of oversized
loads while minimising disruption to public road users.
Ministry Of Transport Regulations On Vehicle Inspection And Licensing (2005)

These regulations, established by the Ministry of Transport in 2005, outline mandatory procedures
for vehicle inspections and licensing to maintain safety and operational reliability. They ensure that
all vehicles involved in transport activities meet required safety standards before operating on public
roads
Law On Road Transport (Law No. 477)
Establishes the overarching legal framework for road transport operations in Tajikistan, detailing
operator responsibilities, safety standards, and operational protocols. This law ensures all transport
activities comply with national road transport regulations and legal requirements.
International Standards And E&S Guidelines
UNECE Transport Conventions
Tajikistan’s participation in UNECE conventions ensures alignment with international standards for
vehicle safety, operational protocols, and environmental management. Key provisions include:



Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment
Project No.: project number | Our Ref No.: Project REF                                     October 2025
Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 261
        Requirements for vehicle safety features (e.g., stability controls for oversized loads).
        Best practices for managing road hazards, such as landslides and low-visibility conditions.
World Bank Environmental And Social Framework (ESF)
ESS1: Assessment and Management of Environmental and Social Risks and Impacts: Provides a
framework for identifying and mitigating risks associated with transport operations.
ESS3: Resource Efficiency and Pollution Prevention and Management: Ensures that traffic-related
environmental impacts such as vehicle emissions, fuel consumption, and hazardous material
spillages are minimized through resource-efficient practices and pollution control measures.
ESS4: Community Health and Safety: Focuses on minimising risks to local communities, particularly
related to road safety and hazardous materials transport.
World Bank Guidelines And Notes
General EHS Guidelines (2007): Community Health and Safety: Outlines best practices for road
safety and managing risks to public health from transport activities.
Good Practice Note: Road Safety: Provides strategies to integrate road safety measures into
transport planning and logistics operations.
Guidance Note for Borrowers: Environmental & Social Framework for IPF Operations – ESS3:
Resource Efficiency and Pollution Prevention and Management
Provides practical guidance for minimizing environmental impacts from project-related traffic,
including controlling vehicle emissions, promoting fuel efficiency, and managing hazardous materials
such as fuel and lubricants to prevent spills and contamination.
Guidance Note for Borrowers: Environmental & Social Framework for IPF Operations – ESS4:
Community Health and Safety
Outlines practical guidance for integrating traffic safety measures into project planning, particularly in
high-risk areas near settlements or public roads.


United Nations Global Plan For The Decade Of Action For Road Safety 2021–2030

Offers a roadmap for reducing road traffic risks through safe system principles, particularly for
oversized and complex transport operations.
Permits And Approvals
Special Travel Certificate

Mandated under Government Resolution 779/2006, this certificate authorises the transit of oversized
loads, ensuring compliance with safety protocols and route viability assessments.
Oversized Load Permits
Issued by the Ministry of Transport, these permits authorise the movement of oversized cargo along
designated routes. They ensure regulatory compliance and minimise disruption to public road users.

Environmental Approvals
Transport operations must adhere to World Bank environmental guidelines and secure applicable
permits to manage emissions, reduce environmental impacts, and ensure safe waste management
practices.


TRAFFIC RISK ASSESSMENT AND HAZARD MITIGATION STRATEGY
Key risks include road safety concerns, pedestrian and community safety, road infrastructure
degradation, driver delays, and specific risks from the transportation of hazardous and oversized
loads. While ongoing road upgrades along sections of the M41 highway and improved infrastructure
are expected to mitigate some risks, targeted measures are required to address remaining
challenges effectively.
Key Risk Areas
Community And Pedestrian Safety
Increased traffic volumes and the presence of heavy goods vehicles (HGVs) along the M41 highway
and surrounding rural areas pose significant safety risks to communities. These risks are heightened
in areas where road conditions are substandard, and formal pedestrian crossings or separation
between vehicles and pedestrians with dedicated pedestrian walkways are insufficient. The
presence of such walkways and crossings can improve safety for vulnerable groups such as
children and older people.
Road Infrastructure And Condition

High traffic volumes, particularly from heavy goods vehicle (HGV)s and oversized loads, accelerate
road degradation, leading to unsafe conditions for all users. Specific sections of the M41 highway,
such as the stretch between Kalaynay and Obigarm, require targeted upgrades due to frequent
potholes, sharp turns, and steep gradients lacking safety barriers.
Realigned sections of the M41 between Obigarm-Nurobod are expected to alleviate some of these
risks with improved capacity and safety features.
Oversized And Hazardous Loads

The transport of hazardous materials and abnormal loads for the Project presents unique
challenges. Movements require compliance with national regulations, Ministry of Transport permits,
and coordination with local authorities for safe passage and consistent with the WB ESF and GIIP.
Driver Behaviour And Delay

Extended transport routes and limited infrastructure contribute to driver fatigue, unsafe practices,
and potential delays, particularly at intersections, site entrances, and high-traffic urban zones like
near the main gate in Rogun City. Worker shift changeovers can exacerbate congestion due to the
heavy reliance on private vehicles and taxis in the absence of organised transport solutions, and
vehicles parked on roadside verges outside the gate can delay passing traffic.




Rogun Hydropower Project – Updated Environmental and Social Impact Assessment

Project Management Group, JSC “Rogun HPP”, DFZ                                               Page | 263
Traffic Risk Management Framework
Alignment With Tajikistan Legislation
The Traffic Management Framework complies with Tajikistan’s transport laws to ensure safe and
efficient project-related vehicle operations. Oversized load transport, governed by Government
Resolution 779/2006, requires permits from the Ministry of Transport and coordination with the State
Traffic Police to ensure safe passage along designated routes.
Vehicles must meet safety standards as per the Ministry of Transport Regulations on Vehicle
Inspection and Licensing (2005). Transport activities follow the Code of Road Transport (Law No.
1689) and Law on Road Transport (Law No. 477), ensuring driver licensing, vehicle compliance, and
adherence to road safety protocols. The Law "On Roads and Road Activities" (Article 46) mandates
secure transport for hazardous materials, while the Rules for Passing by Highways of Vehicles with
Loads Exceeding Established Norms (2006) require route assessments and local authority
coordination for heavy or oversized loads.
Risk Management Principles

Effective off-site traffic risk management relies on the following principles:
       Route Planning: Identifying and assessing transport routes to ensure their suitability for
        project-related traffic, particularly for oversized and hazardous loads.
       Mitigation of Community Impacts: Minimising risks to pedestrians, local residents, and
        public road users by implementing traffic control measures and maintaining open
        communication with affected communities.
       Regulatory Compliance: Ensuring all transport activities meet national regulatory
        requirements, including obtaining permits for oversized loads and coordinating with traffic
        authorities.
       Collaboration: Working with the Ministry of Transport, State Traffic Police, local authorities,
        and nearby communities and settlements to maintain safe and efficient transport operations.
        This includes addressing local concerns, planning traffic management measures to reduce
        disruptions, and incorporating feedback into transport strategies.
Hierarchy Of Control

The hierarchy of control provides a structured approach to managing off-site traffic risks, prioritising
measures that deliver the highest levels of protection and reliability. These include:
       Elimination: Reducing unnecessary transport activities by consolidating loads and
        scheduling deliveries to avoid peak traffic periods.
       Substitution: Employing safer transportation methods where possible, such as using
        escorted convoys for hazardous or oversized loads.
       Engineering Controls: Upgrading infrastructure along key routes, such as repairing
        damaged road sections and installing reflective markers and warning signage.
       Administrative Controls: Enforcing traffic management policies, including mandatory use
        of permits, pre-approved routes, and clear transport schedules.
       PPE and Visibility: Ensuring relevant workers involved in off-site traffic management wear
        high-visibility clothing and have access to appropriate safety equipment (e.g. traffic
        marshals, loading/unlading activities etc).
